"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Absolute_location"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Absolute location"">absolute location</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The particular <a href=""#location""><span title=""See entry on this page at § location"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">location</span></a> of a point on the Earth's surface that can be expressed by a grid reference such as <a href=""#latitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § latitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">latitude</span></a> and <a href=""#longitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § longitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">longitude</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-OERI_1996_1-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-OERI_1996-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Accessibility"" title=""Accessibility"">accessibility</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A locational characteristic that permits a place to be reached by the efforts of those at other places.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"accessibility resource"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A naturally emergent landscape form that eases communication between areas.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Active_volcano"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Active volcano"">active volcano</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A <a href=""#volcano""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volcano"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volcano</span></a> that is currently erupting, or one that has erupted within the last 10,000 years (the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocene"" title=""Holocene"">Holocene</a>) or during recorded history.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tributary"" title=""Tributary"">affluent</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#tributary""><span title=""See entry on this page at § tributary"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">tributary</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agricultural_geography"" title=""Agricultural geography"">agricultural geography</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A sub-discipline of geography which studies the spatial relationships between humans and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agriculture"" title=""Agriculture"">agriculture</a> and the cultural, political, and environmental processes that lead to parts of the Earth's surface being transformed by humans through <a href=""#primary_sector""><span title=""See entry on this page at § primary sector"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">primary sector</span></a> activities into agricultural landscapes.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alluvial_fan"" title=""Alluvial fan"">alluvial fan</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A distinctly triangular, fan-shaped deposit of sediment transported by water, often referred to as <a href=""#alluvium""><span title=""See entry on this page at § alluvium"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">alluvium</span></a>. Alluvial fans usually form at the base of <a href=""#mountain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mountain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mountains</span></a>, where high-velocity rivers or streams meet a relatively flat area and lose the energy needed to carry large quantities of sediment, which ultimately spreads out in all available directions. They tend to be larger and more obvious in arid regions.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alluvial_plain"" title=""Alluvial plain"">alluvial plain</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A wide, flat, gently sloping <a href=""#plain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § plain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">plain</span></a> created by the long-term deposition of <a href=""#alluvium""><span title=""See entry on this page at § alluvium"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">alluvium</span></a> from one or more <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">rivers</span></a> flowing from <a href=""#highland""><span title=""See entry on this page at § highland"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">highland</span></a> regions, and typically characterized by various <a href=""#fluvial""><span title=""See entry on this page at § fluvial"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">fluvial</span></a> landforms such as <a href=""#braided_stream""><span title=""See entry on this page at § braided stream"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">braided streams</span></a>, <a href=""#fluvial_terrace""><span title=""See entry on this page at § fluvial terrace"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">terraces</span></a>, and <a href=""#meander""><span title=""See entry on this page at § meander"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">meanders</span></a>. Alluvial plains encompass the larger area over which a river's <a href=""#floodplain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § floodplain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">floodplain</span></a> has shifted through geological time.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alluvial_soil"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Alluvial soil"">alluvial soils</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Soils deposited through the action of moving water. These soils lack <a href=""#soil_horizon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § soil horizon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">horizons</span></a> and are usually highly fertile.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alluvium"" title=""Alluvium"">alluvium</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Clay, silt, gravel, or similar detrital material deposited by running water.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Altitude"" title=""Altitude"">altitude</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The height of an object in the <a href=""#atmosphere""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atmosphere"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atmosphere</span></a> above <a href=""#sea_level""><span title=""See entry on this page at § sea level"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sea level</span></a>. Compare <i><a href=""#elevation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § elevation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">elevation</span></a></i>.<sup id=""cite_ref-OERI_1996_1-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-OERI_1996-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antarctic"" title=""Antarctic"">Antarctic</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The region of the Earth that is south of the <a href=""#antarctic_Circle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Antarctic Circle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Antarctic Circle</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antarctic_Circle"" title=""Antarctic Circle"">Antarctic Circle</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The southernmost of the Earth's two <a href=""#polar_circle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § polar circle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">polar circles</span></a> of <a href=""#latitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § latitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">latitude</span></a>, south of which the sun appears above the <a href=""#horizon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § horizon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">horizon</span></a> for 24 continuous hours at least once per year (and is therefore visible at midnight) and also appears at least partially below the horizon for 24 continuous hours at least once per year (and is therefore not visible at noon). Its latitude is approximately 66°33′47.1″ south of the <a href=""#equator""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Equator"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Equator</span></a>. Contrast <i><a href=""#arctic_Circle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Arctic Circle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Arctic Circle</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthropization"" title=""Anthropization"">anthropization</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The conversion of open spaces, landscapes, and natural environments by human action.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anticline"" title=""Anticline"">anticline</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A geological <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fold_(geology)"" title=""Fold (geology)"">fold</a> that has an arch-like <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Convex_curve"" title=""Convex curve"">convex</a> shape and its oldest <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bed_(geology)"" title=""Bed (geology)"">beds</a> near its center, often visible at the Earth's surface in exposed <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stratum"" title=""Stratum"">rock strata</a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antimeridian"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Antimeridian"">antimeridian</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The line of <a href=""#longitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § longitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">longitude</span></a> exactly 180 degrees east or west of the <a href=""#prime_Meridian""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Prime Meridian"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Prime Meridian</span></a>, with which it forms a <a href=""#great_circle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § great circle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">great circle</span></a> dividing the Earth into the <a href=""#eastern_Hemisphere""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Eastern Hemisphere"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Eastern</span></a> and <a href=""#western_Hemisphere""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Western Hemisphere"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Western Hemispheres</span></a>. It is used as the approximate basis for the <a href=""#international_Date_Line""><span title=""See entry on this page at § International Date Line"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">International Date Line</span></a> because it mostly passes through the open waters of the Pacific Ocean.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antipodes"" title=""Antipodes"">antipodes</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any pair of points on the Earth's surface that are <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diameter"" title=""Diameter"">diametrically</a> opposite to each other, such that a straight line connecting them would pass through the Earth's center. Such points are as far away from each other as possible, with the <a href=""#great-circle_distance""><span title=""See entry on this page at § great-circle distance"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">great-circle distance</span></a> between them being approximately 20,000 kilometres (12,000&#160;mi).</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apparent_place"" title=""Apparent place"">apparent place</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The apparent position of an object in space as seen by an observer, which, because of physical and geometric effects, may differ from the object's true position.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aquifer"" title=""Aquifer"">aquifer</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An underground layer of <a href=""#groundwater""><span title=""See entry on this page at § groundwater"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">water-bearing</span></a> permeable rock, rock fractures, or unconsolidated materials such as gravel, sand, or silt.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archipelago"" title=""Archipelago"">archipelago</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A collection of <a href=""#island""><span title=""See entry on this page at § island"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">islands</span></a> in a sea.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ar%C3%AAte"" title=""Arête"">arête</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A sharp, narrow mountain <a href=""#ridge""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ridge"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ridge</span></a>, often resulting from the erosive activity of alpine <a href=""#glacier""><span title=""See entry on this page at § glacier"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">glaciers</span></a> flowing in adjacent <a href=""#valley""><span title=""See entry on this page at § valley"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">valleys</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arroyo_(creek)"" title=""Arroyo (creek)"">arroyo</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A deep <a href=""#gully""><span title=""See entry on this page at § gully"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">gully</span></a> cut by a stream that flows only part of the year; a dry <a href=""#gulch""><span title=""See entry on this page at § gulch"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">gulch</span></a>. The term is used primarily in <a href=""#desert""><span title=""See entry on this page at § desert"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">desert</span></a> areas.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arctic"" title=""Arctic"">Arctic</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The region of the Earth that is north of the <a href=""#arctic_Circle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Arctic Circle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Arctic Circle</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arctic_Circle"" title=""Arctic Circle"">Arctic Circle</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The northernmost of the Earth's two <a href=""#polar_circle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § polar circle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">polar circles</span></a> of <a href=""#latitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § latitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">latitude</span></a>, north of which the sun appears above the <a href=""#horizon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § horizon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">horizon</span></a> for 24 continuous hours at least once per year (and is therefore visible at midnight) and also appears at least partially below the horizon for 24 continuous hours at least once per year (and is therefore not visible at noon). Its latitude is approximately 66°33′47.1″ north of the <a href=""#equator""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Equator"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Equator</span></a>. Contrast <i><a href=""#antarctic_Circle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Antarctic Circle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Antarctic Circle</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volcanic_ash"" title=""Volcanic ash"">ash</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Fragments of <a href=""#lava""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lava"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lava</span></a> or rock less than <span class=""frac nowrap""><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>3</sub></span> centimetre (0.13&#160;in) in diameter that have been ejected into the atmosphere by a <a href=""#volcano""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volcano"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volcanic</span></a> explosion.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlantic_Seaboard_fall_line"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Atlantic Seaboard fall line"">Atlantic Seaboard fall line</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The physiographic border between the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Piedmont_(United_States)"" title=""Piedmont (United States)"">Piedmont</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlantic_coastal_plain"" title=""Atlantic coastal plain"">Atlantic coastal plain</a> regions of eastern North America. The name derives from the river rapids and falls that occur as the water flows from the hard rocks of the higher piedmont onto the softer rocks of the coastal plain.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-6"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlas"" title=""Atlas"">atlas</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A bound collection of <a href=""#map""><span title=""See entry on this page at § map"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">maps</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-OERI_1996_1-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-OERI_1996-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atmosphere"" title=""Atmosphere"">atmosphere</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The mixture of gases, aerosols, solid particles, and water vapor that envelops the Earth.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atoll"" title=""Atoll"">atoll</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A ring-shaped <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coral_reef"" title=""Coral reef"">coral reef</a> that partially or completely encircles a <a href=""#lagoon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lagoon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lagoon</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ayre_(landform)"" title=""Ayre (landform)"">ayre</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Another name for a <a href=""#shingle_beach""><span title=""See entry on this page at § shingle beach"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">shingle beach</span></a> or other gravel-covered <a href=""#spit""><span title=""See entry on this page at § spit"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">spit</span></a>, <a href=""#bar""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bar"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bar</span></a>, or <a href=""#tombolo""><span title=""See entry on this page at § tombolo"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">tombolo</span></a>, used primarily in the <a href=""#archipelago""><span title=""See entry on this page at § archipelago"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">archipelagos</span></a> of northern <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scotland"" title=""Scotland"">Scotland</a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azimuth"" title=""Azimuth"">azimuth</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The angle formed between a reference vector (often <a href=""#magnetic_north""><span title=""See entry on this page at § magnetic north"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">magnetic north</span></a>) and a line from the observer to a point of interest projected perpendicularly to the <a href=""#zenith""><span title=""See entry on this page at § zenith"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">zenith</span></a> on the same <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plane_of_reference"" title=""Plane of reference"">plane</a> as the reference vector. Azimuth is usually measured in <a href=""#degree""><span title=""See entry on this page at § degree"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">degrees</span></a> and can be determined with a <a href=""#compass""><span title=""See entry on this page at § compass"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">compass</span></a>.</dd>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backwater_(river)"" title=""Backwater (river)"">backwater</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A part of a <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a> in which there is little or no current.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Badlands"" title=""Badlands"">badlands</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An area of rugged or irregular <a href=""#topography""><span title=""See entry on this page at § topography"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">topography</span></a> resulting from extensive wind and water erosion of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sedimentary_rock"" title=""Sedimentary rock"">sedimentary rock</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-7"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bajada_(geography)"" title=""Bajada (geography)"">bajada</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also spelled <b>bahada</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A series of adjacent <a href=""#alluvial_fan""><span title=""See entry on this page at § alluvial fan"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">alluvial fans</span></a> coalescing in a basin at the foot of a <a href=""#mountain_range""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mountain range"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mountain range</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(river_morphology)"" title=""Bar (river morphology)"">bar</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An elevated region of sediment such as sand or gravel which has been deposited by the flow of a <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a> or other moving body of water. See also <i><a href=""#shoal""><span title=""See entry on this page at § shoal"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">shoal</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barrier_ridge"" title=""Barrier ridge"">barrier ridge</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any steep, unnavigable <a href=""#ridge""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ridge"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ridge</span></a> or <a href=""#escarpment""><span title=""See entry on this page at § escarpment"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">escarpment</span></a> isolating one <a href=""#terrain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § terrain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">terrain</span></a> from another.</dd>
"
"base level"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The lowest level to which a <a href=""#stream""><span title=""See entry on this page at § stream"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">stream</span></a> can erode its <a href=""#streambed""><span title=""See entry on this page at § streambed"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bed</span></a>. The ultimate base level of all streams is the <a href=""#sea""><span title=""See entry on this page at § sea"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sea</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-8"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(geology)"" title=""Depression (geology)"">basin</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#depression""><span title=""See entry on this page at § depression"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">depression</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Batholith"" title=""Batholith"">batholith</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A very large body of <a href=""#igneous_rock""><span title=""See entry on this page at § igneous rock"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">igneous rock</span></a>, usually <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Granite"" title=""Granite"">granite</a>, which has been exposed by <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erosion"" title=""Erosion"">erosion</a> of the overlying rock.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-9"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bathymetry"" title=""Bathymetry"">bathymetry</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;The measurement of water depth, mainly of <a href=""#sea""><span title=""See entry on this page at § sea"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">seas</span></a> and <a href=""#ocean""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ocean"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">oceans</span></a> but sometimes of deep <a href=""#lake""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lake"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lakes</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;The study and depiction of the physical features or <a href=""#terrain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § terrain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">relief</span></a> of the <a href=""#seabed""><span title=""See entry on this page at § seabed"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">floor</span></a> of a lake or ocean. In this sense bathymetry is considered the underwater equivalent of <a href=""#hypsometry""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hypsometry"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hypsometry</span></a> or <a href=""#topography""><span title=""See entry on this page at § topography"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">topography</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bay"" title=""Bay"">bay</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A <a href=""#coast""><span title=""See entry on this page at § coast"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">coastal</span></a> body of water that is directly connected to but recessed from a larger body of water, such as an <a href=""#ocean""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ocean"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ocean</span></a>, <a href=""#sea""><span title=""See entry on this page at § sea"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sea</span></a>, <a href=""#lake""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lake"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lake</span></a>, or another bay. The land surrounding a bay often shelters it from strong winds and waves, making bays ideal places for ports and harbors. Bays are sometimes found adjacent to <a href=""#headland""><span title=""See entry on this page at § headland"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">headlands</span></a> on <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discordant_coastline"" title=""Discordant coastline"">discordant coastlines</a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beach"" title=""Beach"">beach</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A landform along the <a href=""#coast""><span title=""See entry on this page at § coast"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">shoreline</span></a> of an <a href=""#ocean""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ocean"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ocean</span></a>, <a href=""#sea""><span title=""See entry on this page at § sea"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sea</span></a>, <a href=""#lake""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lake"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lake</span></a>, or <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a> with a loose surface of sand, gravel, shingle, pebbles, shells, stones, or coral.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bearing_(navigation)"" title=""Bearing (navigation)"">bearing</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The direction or position of an object, or the direction of an object's movement, relative to a fixed point. It is typically measured in <a href=""#degree""><span title=""See entry on this page at § degree"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">degrees</span></a> and can be determined with a <a href=""#compass""><span title=""See entry on this page at § compass"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">compass</span></a>. By convention, <a href=""#north_Magnetic_Pole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § North Magnetic Pole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">magnetic north</span></a> is defined as having a bearing of zero degrees.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bedrock"" title=""Bedrock"">bedrock</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The solid rock in the Earth's <a href=""#crust""><span title=""See entry on this page at § crust"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">crust</span></a> that underlies all soil and other loose material; the rock material that breaks down eventually to form soil.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-10"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bight_(geography)"" title=""Bight (geography)"">bight</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A bend or curve in a coastline, river, or other geographical feature typically indicating an especially large, open <a href=""#bay""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bay"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bay</span></a> that is shallower than a <a href=""#sound""><span title=""See entry on this page at § sound"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sound</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biodiversity"" title=""Biodiversity"">biological diversity</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called <b>biodiversity</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A concept recognizing the variety of life forms in an area of the Earth and the ecological interdependence of these life forms.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-11"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biogeography"" title=""Biogeography"">biogeography</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The study of the distribution of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biology"" title=""Biology"">biological</a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Species"" title=""Species"">species</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecosystems"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Ecosystems"">ecosystems</a> in geographic space and through geological time.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biosphere"" title=""Biosphere"">biosphere</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The realm of all living things.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biota_(ecology)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Biota (ecology)"">biota</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The animal and plant life of a region considered as a total ecological entity.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-12"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blowout_(geomorphology)"" title=""Blowout (geomorphology)"">blowout</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A sandy <a href=""#depression""><span title=""See entry on this page at § depression"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">depression</span></a> formed when <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wind"" title=""Wind"">wind</a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wind_erosion"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Wind erosion"">erodes</a> into patches of bare sand on otherwise vegetation-stabilized <a href=""#dune""><span title=""See entry on this page at § dune"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sand dunes</span></a> at the margins of coastal and arid ecosystems.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bocage"" title=""Bocage"">bocage</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A landscape of mixed woodland and <a href=""#pasture""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pasture"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pasture</span></a>, with fields and winding country lanes sunken between low, narrow ridges and banks surmounted by tall, thick <a href=""#hedgerow""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hedgerow"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hedgerows</span></a>, especially as found in rural parts of western Europe.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Body_of_water"" title=""Body of water"">body of water</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any significant accumulation of water, either natural or artificial, on the surface of the Earth. Bodies of water may hold or contain water, as with <a href=""#lake""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lake"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lakes</span></a> and <a href=""#ocean""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ocean"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">oceans</span></a>, or they may collect and move water from one place to another, as with <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">rivers</span></a>, <a href=""#stream""><span title=""See entry on this page at § stream"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">streams</span></a>, and other <a href=""#watercourse""><span title=""See entry on this page at § watercourse"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">watercourses</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bog"" title=""Bog"">bog</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>mire</b>, <b>quagmire</b>, or <b><a href=""#muskeg""><span title=""See entry on this page at § muskeg"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">muskeg</span></a></b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A type of <a href=""#wetland""><span title=""See entry on this page at § wetland"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">wetland</span></a> which accumulates deposits of dead plant material, especially <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moss"" title=""Moss"">mosses</a>, known as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peat"" title=""Peat"">peat</a>. Bogs occur where the water at the ground surface is acidic and low in dissolved nutrients. They are one of four main types of wetland.</dd>
"
"bootheel"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#salient""><span title=""See entry on this page at § salient"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">salient</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Border"" title=""Border"">border</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The geographical boundary of a political entity or legal jurisdiction, such as a <a href=""#country""><span title=""See entry on this page at § country"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">country</span></a>, <a href=""#state""><span title=""See entry on this page at § state"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">state</span></a>, or other <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subnational_entity"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Subnational entity"">subnational entity</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-OERI_1996_1-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-OERI_1996-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bornhardt"" title=""Bornhardt"">bornhardt</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A bald, steep-sided, dome-shaped hill, mountain, or rock <a href=""#outcrop""><span title=""See entry on this page at § outcrop"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">outcropping</span></a> at least 30 metres (98&#160;ft) in height and several hundred meters in width. Compare <i><a href=""#inselberg""><span title=""See entry on this page at § inselberg"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">inselberg</span></a></i>, <i><a href=""#tor""><span title=""See entry on this page at § tor"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">tor</span></a></i>, and <i><a href=""#nubbin""><span title=""See entry on this page at § nubbin"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">nubbin</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Borough"" title=""Borough"">borough</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A type of <a href=""#administrative_division""><span title=""See entry on this page at § administrative division"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">administrative subdivision</span></a> in certain English-speaking parts of the world. Though traditionally used to refer to a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fortress"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Fortress"">fortress</a> or a walled <a href=""#town""><span title=""See entry on this page at § town"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">town</span></a>, modern usage of the term can variably refer to any town with its own local self-government, a formal or informal subdivision of a large <a href=""#metropolis""><span title=""See entry on this page at § metropolis"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">metropolis</span></a> (as in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_City"" title=""New York City"">New York City</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/London"" title=""London"">London</a>), or an entire administrative <a href=""#region""><span title=""See entry on this page at § region"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">region</span></a> (as in the U.S. state of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alaska"" title=""Alaska"">Alaska</a>).</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Box_canyon"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Box canyon"">box canyon</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A short, narrow <a href=""#canyon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § canyon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">canyon</span></a> with steep walls on three sides, allowing entry and exit only through the mouth of the canyon.</dd>
"
"break-in-bulk point"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A transfer point on a transport route where the mode of transport or type of carrier changes and where large-volume shipments are reduced in size. For example, goods may be unloaded from a ship and transferred to trucks at an ocean port.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-13"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breakwater_(structure)"" title=""Breakwater (structure)"">breakwater</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any man-made structure built on the <a href=""#coast""><span title=""See entry on this page at § coast"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">coast</span></a> of a body of water, typically the <a href=""#sea""><span title=""See entry on this page at § sea"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sea</span></a>, in order to reduce the intensity of wave action in an area adjacent to the shore, thereby providing safe harbourage for human activities in the inshore waters. Breakwaters may also be designed to protect the coastline from <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coastal_erosion"" title=""Coastal erosion"">coastal erosion</a> and <a href=""#longshore_drift""><span title=""See entry on this page at § longshore drift"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">longshore drift</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Built_environment"" title=""Built environment"">built environment</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The human-made spaces that provide the setting for human activity, in which people live, work, and recreate on a day-to-day basis.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Butte"" title=""Butte"">butte</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An isolated <a href=""#hill""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hill"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hill</span></a> or <a href=""#mountain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mountain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mountain</span></a> with steep or precipitous sides, usually having a smaller summit area than a <a href=""#mesa""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mesa"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mesa</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-14"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cadastre"" title=""Cadastre"">cadastre</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also spelled <b>cadaster</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A type of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_registration"" title=""Land registration"">parcel-based</a> land recording system containing a comprehensive record of interests in individual units of land within a <a href=""#country""><span title=""See entry on this page at § country"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">country</span></a> or other polity, usually including a geometric description of each parcel's physical location, dimensions, and <a href=""#metes_and_bounds""><span title=""See entry on this page at § metes and bounds"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">boundaries</span></a> that is linked to legal information detailing the nature of the interests (e.g. rights, restrictions, and responsibilities), the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_tenure"" title=""Land tenure"">ownership</a> or control of those interests, and the economic value of the land and its improvements. The cadastre is a fundamental source of data used in resolving disputes between landowners.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calanque"" title=""Calanque"">calanque</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A narrow, steep-sided <a href=""#valley""><span title=""See entry on this page at § valley"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">valley</span></a> surrounding an <a href=""#inlet""><span title=""See entry on this page at § inlet"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">inlet</span></a> formed in <a href=""#karst""><span title=""See entry on this page at § karst"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">karstic</span></a> regions along the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea"" title=""Mediterranean Sea"">Mediterranean</a> coast, either by fluvial erosion or the collapse of the roof of a <a href=""#cave""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cave"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cave</span></a> that has been subsequently partially submerged by a rise in sea level.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caldera"" title=""Caldera"">caldera</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A large, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cauldron"" title=""Cauldron"">cauldron</a>-shaped <a href=""#depression""><span title=""See entry on this page at § depression"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">depression</span></a> that forms through the subsidence and collapse of a ground surface following the evacuation of an underlying <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magma_chamber"" title=""Magma chamber"">magma chamber</a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canal"" title=""Canal"">canal</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A navigable artificial water <a href=""#channel""><span title=""See entry on this page at § channel"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">channel</span></a>, usually built as a conduit for human activity.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canyon"" title=""Canyon"">canyon</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>gorge</b> or spelled <b>cañon</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A deep cleft between <a href=""#cliff""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cliff"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cliffs</span></a> or <a href=""#escarpment""><span title=""See entry on this page at § escarpment"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">escarpments</span></a>, or a rift between two mountain peaks, resulting from <a href=""#weathering""><span title=""See entry on this page at § weathering"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">weathering</span></a> and the erosive activity of a <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a> over long periods of geologic time.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cape_(geography)"" title=""Cape (geography)"">cape</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A large <a href=""#headland""><span title=""See entry on this page at § headland"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">headland</span></a> or <a href=""#promontory""><span title=""See entry on this page at § promontory"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">promontory</span></a> extending into a body of water, usually a sea or ocean.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caprock"" title=""Caprock"">caprock</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stratum"" title=""Stratum"">stratum</a> of erosion-resistant <a href=""#sedimentary_rock""><span title=""See entry on this page at § sedimentary rock"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sedimentary rock</span></a> (usually <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Limestone"" title=""Limestone"">limestone</a>) found in arid areas. Caprock forms the top layer of most <a href=""#mesa""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mesa"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mesas</span></a> and <a href=""#butte""><span title=""See entry on this page at § butte"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">buttes</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-15"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cardinal_directions"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Cardinal directions"">cardinal directions</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The set of four primary directions used in <a href=""#cartography""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cartography"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cartography</span></a> and <a href=""#navigation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § navigation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">navigation</span></a>: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North"" title=""North"">north</a> (N), <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South"" title=""South"">south</a> (S), <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East"" title=""East"">east</a> (E), and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West"" title=""West"">west</a> (W). Together they form the primary divisions of the <a href=""#compass_rose""><span title=""See entry on this page at § compass rose"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">compass rose</span></a>. They can be further subdivided into the <a href=""#intercardinal_directions""><span title=""See entry on this page at § intercardinal directions"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">intercardinal directions</span></a> and <a href=""#secondary-intercardinal_directions""><span title=""See entry on this page at § secondary-intercardinal directions"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">secondary-intercardinal directions</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carrying_capacity"" title=""Carrying capacity"">carrying capacity</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The total number of human beings that an area can support given the quality of the natural environment and the level of technology of the population.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-16"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cartography"" title=""Cartography"">cartography</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The study and practice of making <a href=""#map""><span title=""See entry on this page at § map"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">maps</span></a> and charts. A person who draws or makes maps or charts is called a <i>cartographer</i>.<sup id=""cite_ref-OERI_1996_1-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-OERI_1996-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cartogram"" title=""Cartogram"">cartogram</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A map in which some thematic mapping variable, such as travel time, population, or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gross_national_product"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Gross national product"">gross national product</a>, is substituted for traditional measures of land area or distance such that the geometry or space of the map is distorted in order to convey and emphasize the information of the alternate variable.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cave"" title=""Cave"">cave</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any naturally hollow underground space large enough for a person to enter.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cavern"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Cavern"">cavern</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A type of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solutional_cave"" title=""Solutional cave"">solutional</a> <a href=""#cave""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cave"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cave</span></a> that is formed in soluble rock with the ability to grow <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speleothem"" title=""Speleothem"">speleothems</a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cay"" title=""Cay"">cay</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A small, sandy, low-elevation <a href=""#island""><span title=""See entry on this page at § island"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">island</span></a> on the surface of an otherwise submerged <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coral_reef"" title=""Coral reef"">coral reef</a>; a type of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coral_island"" title=""Coral island"">coral island</a>. Compare <i><a href=""#atoll""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atoll"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atoll</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celestial_pole"" title=""Celestial pole"">celestial pole</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Either of the two imaginary points in the sky at which an indefinitely extended projection of the Earth's axis of rotation intersects the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celestial_sphere"" title=""Celestial sphere"">celestial sphere</a>. As the Earth rotates upon its axis, the north and south celestial poles remain permanently fixed in the sky (directly overhead to observers at the <a href=""#north_Geographic_Pole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § North Geographic Pole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">North Pole</span></a> and <a href=""#south_Geographic_Pole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § South Geographic Pole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">South Pole</span></a>, respectively), and all other points appear to rotate around them.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cenote"" title=""Cenote"">cenote</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A natural pit or <a href=""#sinkhole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § sinkhole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sinkhole</span></a> resulting from the collapse of limestone <a href=""#bedrock""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bedrock"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bedrock</span></a> which exposes <a href=""#groundwater""><span title=""See entry on this page at § groundwater"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">groundwater</span></a> underneath.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_business_district"" title=""Central business district"">central business district</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A centrally located commercial business district in an urban area, typically containing a concentration of office and retail activities.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-17"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Census-designated_place"" title=""Census-designated place"">census-designated place</a> (CDP)"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A concentration of population identified by the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau"" title=""United States Census Bureau"">United States Census Bureau</a> for statistical purposes.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Channel_(geography)"" title=""Channel (geography)"">channel</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>strait</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;A <a href=""#waterway""><span title=""See entry on this page at § waterway"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">waterway</span></a> separating two relatively close landmasses.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;Any narrow <a href=""#body_of_water""><span title=""See entry on this page at § body of water"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">body of water</span></a> that connects two larger bodies of water.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">3.&#160;&#160;The deepest part of a shallow body of water, often used as a passageway for large ships.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chaparral"" title=""Chaparral"">chaparral</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A class of terrestrial vegetation characterized by dense, impenetrable thickets of shrubs or dwarf trees.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-18"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"chimney"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#salient""><span title=""See entry on this page at § salient"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">salient</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chine"" title=""Chine"">chine</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A steep-sided <a href=""#coast""><span title=""See entry on this page at § coast"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">coastal</span></a> <a href=""#canyon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § canyon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">gorge</span></a>, typically of soft eroding cliffs of sandstone or clay, through which a river or stream flows to the sea. The term is used primarily in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_England"" title=""Southern England"">Southern England</a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinook_wind"" title=""Chinook wind"">chinook</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A warm, dry wind experienced along the eastern side of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rocky_Mountains"" title=""Rocky Mountains"">Rocky Mountains</a> in the United States and Canada. Most common in winter and spring, it can result in a rise in temperature of 20&#160;°C (68&#160;°F) in a quarter of an hour.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-19"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chorography"" title=""Chorography"">chorography</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The art of establishing, describing, or mapping a geographic <a href=""#region""><span title=""See entry on this page at § region"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">region</span></a> or <a href=""#district""><span title=""See entry on this page at § district"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">district</span></a>, or more broadly, the representation of space or place.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Choropleth"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Choropleth"">choropleth</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A <a href=""#map""><span title=""See entry on this page at § map"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">map</span></a> showing the distribution of a phenomenon by graded shading which indicates the density per unit area of that phenomenon; the darker the shading, the greater the density.<sup id=""cite_ref-Mayhew_4-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Mayhew-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cinder_cone"" title=""Cinder cone"">cinder cone</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A steep-sided <a href=""#volcano""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volcano"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volcano</span></a> formed by the explosive eruption of cinders that form around a <a href=""#volcanic_vent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volcanic vent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">vent</span></a>. Cinders are <a href=""#lava""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lava"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lava</span></a> fragments about 1 centimetre (0.39&#160;in) in diameter.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circle_of_latitude"" title=""Circle of latitude"">circle of latitude</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#latitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § latitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">latitude</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cirque_(landform)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Cirque (landform)"">cirque</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>corrie</b> or <b>cwm</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">An <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amphitheatre"" title=""Amphitheatre"">amphitheatre</a>-shaped <a href=""#valley""><span title=""See entry on this page at § valley"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">valley</span></a> surrounded on three or more sides by steep, cliff-like slopes and formed by glacial or fluvial erosion.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/City"" title=""City"">city</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A large human <a href=""#settlement""><span title=""See entry on this page at § settlement"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">settlement</span></a>, generally with extensive systems constructed for housing, transportation, sanitation, utilities, and communication.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/City-state"" title=""City-state"">city-state</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A sovereign <a href=""#state""><span title=""See entry on this page at § state"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">state</span></a> or small independent <a href=""#country""><span title=""See entry on this page at § country"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">country</span></a> that usually consists of a single <a href=""#city""><span title=""See entry on this page at § city"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">city</span></a> and its dependent territories.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cliff"" title=""Cliff"">cliff</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any vertical or nearly vertical rock exposure, usually formed by the processes of <a href=""#weathering""><span title=""See entry on this page at § weathering"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">weathering</span></a> and erosion.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climax_vegetation"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Climax vegetation"">climax vegetation</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The vegetation that would exist in an area if growth had proceeded undisturbed for an extended period. This would be the ""final"" collection of plant types that presumably would remain forever, or until the stable conditions were somehow disturbed.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-20"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coast"" title=""Coast"">coast</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>coastline</b> or <b>seashore</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">The area where land meets a <a href=""#sea""><span title=""See entry on this page at § sea"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sea</span></a> or <a href=""#ocean""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ocean"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ocean</span></a>. Coastal zones are regions where the interaction of terrestrial and marine processes occurs. Compare <i><a href=""#shore""><span title=""See entry on this page at § shore"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">shore</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Col"" title=""Col"">col</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>gap</b> or <b>notch</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">The lowest point on a <a href=""#mountain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mountain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mountain</span></a> <a href=""#ridge""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ridge"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ridge</span></a> between two peaks.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colony"" title=""Colony"">colony</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A <a href=""#territory""><span title=""See entry on this page at § territory"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">territory</span></a> under the immediate complete political control of a sovereign <a href=""#metropolitan_state""><span title=""See entry on this page at § metropolitan state"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">metropolitan state</span></a> but otherwise distinct, often geographically, from the state's home territory. Colonies have no international representation independent of the metropolitan state. Compare <i><a href=""#satellite_state""><span title=""See entry on this page at § satellite state"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">satellite state</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commonwealth"" title=""Commonwealth"">commonwealth</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
