"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compass"" title=""Compass"">compass</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An instrument used for <a href=""#navigation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § navigation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">navigation</span></a> and orientation that indicates direction relative to the geographic <a href=""#cardinal_directions""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cardinal directions"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cardinal directions</span></a> by measuring the orientation of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth%27s_magnetic_field"" title=""Earth&#39;s magnetic field"">Earth's magnetic field</a> with respect to the <a href=""#north_Magnetic_Pole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § North Magnetic Pole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">North Magnetic Pole</span></a>. Compasses often display markings for angles or <a href=""#degree""><span title=""See entry on this page at § degree"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">degrees</span></a>, which allow them to show <a href=""#azimuth""><span title=""See entry on this page at § azimuth"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">azimuths</span></a> and <a href=""#bearing""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bearing"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bearings</span></a>, in addition to a <a href=""#compass_rose""><span title=""See entry on this page at § compass rose"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">compass rose</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compass_rose"" title=""Compass rose"">compass rose</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A figure on a <a href=""#compass""><span title=""See entry on this page at § compass"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">compass</span></a>, <a href=""#map""><span title=""See entry on this page at § map"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">map</span></a>, nautical chart, or monument used to display the orientation of the four <a href=""#cardinal_directions""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cardinal directions"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cardinal directions</span></a> — North, East, South, and West — and their intermediate points.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Confluence"" title=""Confluence"">confluence</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The place at which two or more <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">rivers</span></a> or other <a href=""#watercourse""><span title=""See entry on this page at § watercourse"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">watercourses</span></a> flow together to form one larger river or watercourse.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-21"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coniferous"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Coniferous"">coniferous</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Bearing cones; from the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conifer"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Conifer"">conifer</a> family.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-22"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geographic_contiguity"" title=""Geographic contiguity"">contiguity</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The characteristic of a group of neighboring political or geographical divisions not being interrupted by politically unaffiliated land or water. Such divisions are said to be <i>contiguous</i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continent"" title=""Continent"">continent</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">One of several very large, contiguous <a href=""#landmass""><span title=""See entry on this page at § landmass"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">landmasses</span></a> into which the Earth's land area is divided, generally by geographical or political convention rather than any strict criteria.<sup id=""cite_ref-OERI_1996_1-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-OERI_1996-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Geologically, continents correspond largely to areas of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continental_crust"" title=""Continental crust"">continental crust</a> on <a href=""#plate_tectonics""><span title=""See entry on this page at § plate tectonics"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">continental plates</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continental_climate"" title=""Continental climate"">continental climate</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The type of climate found in the interior of the major continents in the middle, or temperate, latitudes. The climate is characterized by a great seasonal variation in temperatures, four distinct seasons, and a relatively small annual precipitation.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-23"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continental_divide"" title=""Continental divide"">continental divide</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The line of high ground that separates the different oceanic <a href=""#drainage_basin""><span title=""See entry on this page at § drainage basin"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">drainage basins</span></a> of a particular <a href=""#continent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § continent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">continent</span></a>. The river systems of a continent on opposite sides of a continental divide flow toward different oceans. See <i><a href=""#drainage_divide""><span title=""See entry on this page at § drainage divide"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">drainage divide</span></a></i>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-24"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continental_shelf"" title=""Continental shelf"">continental shelf</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A portion of a <a href=""#continent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § continent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">continent</span></a> that is submerged beneath an area of relatively shallow water known as a <i>shelf sea</i>. Though continental shelves are usually treated as physiographic provinces of the <a href=""#ocean""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ocean"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ocean</span></a>, they are not part of the deep ocean basin proper but the flooded margins of the continent.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continent"" title=""Continent"">continentality</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The quality of being located on a <a href=""#continent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § continent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">continent</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contour_lines"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Contour lines"">contour lines</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Lines marked on <a href=""#topographic_map""><span title=""See entry on this page at § topographic map"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">topographic maps</span></a> which show the <a href=""#terrain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § terrain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">shape</span></a> and <a href=""#elevation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § elevation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">elevation</span></a> of the land by connecting points of equal elevation.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conurbation"" title=""Conurbation"">conurbation</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An extensive urban area formed when two or more initially separate <a href=""#city""><span title=""See entry on this page at § city"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cities</span></a> coalesce to form a continuous <a href=""#metropolitan_area""><span title=""See entry on this page at § metropolitan area"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">metropolitan area</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-25"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"core area"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The portion of a country that contains its economic, political, intellectual, and cultural focus. It is often the center of creativity and change. See <i><a href=""#hearth""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hearth"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hearth</span></a></i>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-26"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corrasion"" title=""Corrasion"">corrasion</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The process of mechanical <a href=""#erosion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § erosion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">erosion</span></a> of the Earth's surface by the impact or grinding action of particles being transported across it, either by moving water, waves, glaciers, wind or gravity.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tarn_(lake)"" title=""Tarn (lake)"">corrie loch</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#tarn""><span title=""See entry on this page at § tarn"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">tarn</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coulee"" title=""Coulee"">coulee</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A dry <a href=""#canyon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § canyon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">canyon</span></a> eroded by <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pleistocene"" title=""Pleistocene"">Pleistocene</a> floods that cut into the lava beds of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Columbia_Plateau"" title=""Columbia Plateau"">Columbia Plateau</a> in the western United States.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-27"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Couloir"" title=""Couloir"">couloir</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A narrow <a href=""#gully""><span title=""See entry on this page at § gully"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">gully</span></a> with a steep gradient in a mountainous terrain, often enclosed by sheer <a href=""#cliff""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cliff"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cliffs</span></a> and filled with snow or ice even during the summer months.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Country"" title=""Country"">country</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A <a href=""#region""><span title=""See entry on this page at § region"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">region</span></a> identified as a distinct national entity in <a href=""#political_geography""><span title=""See entry on this page at § political geography"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">political geography</span></a>. Compare <i><a href=""#state""><span title=""See entry on this page at § state"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">state</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/County"" title=""County"">county</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A type of subnational division of a <a href=""#country""><span title=""See entry on this page at § country"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">country</span></a> or <a href=""#state""><span title=""See entry on this page at § state"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">federal state</span></a> used for administrative or other purposes.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Course_(navigation)"" title=""Course (navigation)"">course</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/crater"" class=""extiw"" title=""wikt:crater"">crater</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any large, roughly circular <a href=""#depression""><span title=""See entry on this page at § depression"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">depression</span></a>, pit, or hole in the Earth's surface. Craters can be classified into different types based on their ultimate causes; see <i><a href=""#impact_crater""><span title=""See entry on this page at § impact crater"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">impact crater</span></a></i>, <i><a href=""#volcanic_crater""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volcanic crater"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volcanic crater</span></a></i>, and <i><a href=""#pit_crater""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pit crater"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pit crater</span></a></i>.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-6"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volcanic_crater_lake"" title=""Volcanic crater lake"">crater lake</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A <a href=""#lake""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lake"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lake</span></a> that forms in a <a href=""#volcanic_crater""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volcanic crater"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volcanic crater</span></a> or <a href=""#caldera""><span title=""See entry on this page at § caldera"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">caldera</span></a> (such as a <a href=""#maar""><span title=""See entry on this page at § maar"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">maar</span></a>), an <a href=""#impact_crater""><span title=""See entry on this page at § impact crater"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">impact crater</span></a> left by a meteorite, or a crater resulting from a man-made explosion.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crust_(geology)"" title=""Crust (geology)"">crust</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The thin shell of solid material that is the Earth's outermost layer and the outermost component of the <a href=""#lithosphere""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lithosphere"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lithosphere</span></a>. The Earth's crust is generally divided into two distinct types, <a href=""#oceanic_crust""><span title=""See entry on this page at § oceanic crust"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">oceanic crust</span></a> and <a href=""#continental_crust""><span title=""See entry on this page at § continental crust"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">continental crust</span></a>, both of which ""float"" on top of the <a href=""#mantle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mantle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mantle</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-7"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryosphere"" title=""Cryosphere"">cryosphere</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The totality of water in the solid phase on the Earth's surface, including <a href=""#glacier""><span title=""See entry on this page at § glacier"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">glaciers</span></a>; sea, lake, and river <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ice"" title=""Ice"">ice</a>; <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Snow"" title=""Snow"">snow</a>; and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permafrost"" title=""Permafrost"">permafrost</a>. The cryosphere is sometimes considered a subset of the <a href=""#hydrosphere""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hydrosphere"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hydrosphere</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-8"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryoturbation"" title=""Cryoturbation"">cryoturbation</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called <b>frost churning</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">The mixing of materials from various horizons of the soil down to the bedrock due to freezing and thawing.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuesta"" title=""Cuesta"">cuesta</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A long, low ridge with a steep scarp slope and a gentle backslope (dip slope).</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_geography"" title=""Cultural geography"">cultural geography</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A branch of <a href=""#human_geography""><span title=""See entry on this page at § human geography"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">human geography</span></a> which studies the patterns and interactions of human <a href=""#culture""><span title=""See entry on this page at § culture"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">culture</span></a> in relation to the natural environment and the human organization of space.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture"" title=""Culture"">culture</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The accumulated habits, attitudes, and beliefs of a group of people that define for them their general behavior and way of life; the total set of learned activities of a people.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-28"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"culture hearth"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The area from which the <a href=""#culture""><span title=""See entry on this page at § culture"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">culture</span></a> of a group diffused. See <i><a href=""#hearth""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hearth"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hearth</span></a></i>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-29"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cut_bank"" title=""Cut bank"">cut bank</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A continually <a href=""#erosion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § erosion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">eroding</span></a> <a href=""#bank""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bank"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bank</span></a> along a meandering <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a> or <a href=""#stream""><span title=""See entry on this page at § stream"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">stream</span></a> <a href=""#channel""><span title=""See entry on this page at § channel"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">channel</span></a>, especially a bank that has been eroded into a nearly vertical <a href=""#cliff""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cliff"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cliff</span></a>. Cut banks generally form on the outside bend of a deep <a href=""#meander""><span title=""See entry on this page at § meander"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">meander</span></a>, opposite the depositional <a href=""#point_bar""><span title=""See entry on this page at § point bar"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">point bar</span></a> that forms on the inside bend.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cwm_(landform)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Cwm (landform)"">cwm</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#cirque""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cirque"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cirque</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyclopean_stairs"" title=""Cyclopean stairs"">Cyclopean stairs</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A term referring to the longitudinal profile of some <a href=""#glaciation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § glaciation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">glaciated</span></a> <a href=""#valley""><span title=""See entry on this page at § valley"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">valleys</span></a> which have been eroded into a series of consecutive <a href=""#hanging_valley""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hanging valley"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hanging valleys</span></a> resembling stairs.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dale_(landform)"" title=""Dale (landform)"">dale</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Another name for a <a href=""#valley""><span title=""See entry on this page at § valley"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">valley</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dam"" title=""Dam"">dam</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any barrier, either natural or artificial, that stops or restricts the flow of water, either on the surface or underground. Man-made dams are most commonly built to impound rivers or streams, generally to retain water for purposes such as human consumption, irrigation, aquaculture, or power generation (whereas related structures such as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Floodgate"" title=""Floodgate"">floodgates</a> and <a href=""#levee""><span title=""See entry on this page at § levee"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">levees</span></a> are more specifically designed to manage or prevent water flow into particular areas).</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_facto_segregation"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""De facto segregation""><i>de facto</i> segregation</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The spatial and social separation of populations that occurs without legal sanction.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-30"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_jure_segregation"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""De jure segregation""><i>de jure</i> segregation</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The spatial and social separation of populations that occurs because of legal measures.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-31"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Debouch"" title=""Debouch"">debouch</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also spelled <b>debouche</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A place where water runoff from a relatively small, confined space emerges into a much larger, broader space, or where a <a href=""#body_of_water""><span title=""See entry on this page at § body of water"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">body of water</span></a> pours forth from a narrow opening, such as where a stream or river enters a lake or ocean.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deciduous_forest"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Deciduous forest"">deciduous forest</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A forest composed of trees which lose their leaves each year.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-32"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Defile_(geography)"" title=""Defile (geography)"">defile</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A narrow <a href=""#mountain_pass""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mountain pass"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pass</span></a> or <a href=""#canyon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § canyon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">gorge</span></a> between <a href=""#mountain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mountain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mountains</span></a> or <a href=""#hill""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hill"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hills</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Degree_(angle)"" title=""Degree (angle)"">degree</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A unit of angular measure. A circle is divided into 360 degrees, represented by the º symbol. Degrees are used to divide the roughly spherical shape of the Earth for geographic and cartographic purposes.<sup id=""cite_ref-OERI_1996_1-6"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-OERI_1996-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Degree_day"" title=""Degree day"">degree day</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Deviation of one-degree temperature for one day from an arbitrary standard, usually the long-term average temperature for a place.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-33"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dell_(landform)"" title=""Dell (landform)"">dell</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A small, secluded hollow, usually within a grassy, park-like, partially wooded <a href=""#valley""><span title=""See entry on this page at § valley"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">valley</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/River_delta"" title=""River delta"">delta</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A landform at the <a href=""#mouth""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mouth"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mouth</span></a> of a <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a> where the <a href=""#main_stem""><span title=""See entry on this page at § main stem"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">main stem</span></a> splits up into several <a href=""#distributary""><span title=""See entry on this page at § distributary"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">distributaries</span></a>. It is formed from the deposition of the sediment carried by the river as the flow leaves the mouth of the river. Compare <i><a href=""#estuary""><span title=""See entry on this page at § estuary"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">estuary</span></a></i>.<sup id=""cite_ref-NRCS_2018_5-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-NRCS_2018-5"">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demography"" title=""Demography"">demography</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The systematic analysis of <a href=""#population""><span title=""See entry on this page at § population"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">population</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-34"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(geology)"" title=""Depression (geology)"">depression</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any <a href=""#landform""><span title=""See entry on this page at § landform"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">landform</span></a> that is sunken or depressed below the surrounding area. Depressions include an enormous variety of landforms and can form by a number of different mechanisms, including <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erosion"" title=""Erosion"">erosion</a>, ground collapse, <a href=""#plate_tectonics""><span title=""See entry on this page at § plate tectonics"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">tectonic activity</span></a>, <a href=""#volcano""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volcano"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volcanism</span></a>, and <a href=""#impact_crater""><span title=""See entry on this page at § impact crater"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">meteorite impacts</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desert"" title=""Desert"">desert</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An arid, barren area of land where little <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Precipitation"" title=""Precipitation"">precipitation</a> occurs and living conditions are consequently unfavorable for most plant and animal life. Deserts are characterized by exposure of the unprotected ground surface to processes of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denudation"" title=""Denudation"">denudation</a> as well as large variations in temperature between night and day. They are often classified by the amount of precipitation they receive, by their average temperature, by the causes of their <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desertification"" title=""Desertification"">desertification</a>, or by their geographical location.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_elevation_model"" title=""Digital elevation model"">digital elevation model</a> (DEM)"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A three-dimensional computer graphics representation of a geographic <a href=""#terrain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § terrain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">terrain</span></a> surface created from <a href=""#elevation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § elevation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">elevation</span></a> data. DEMs are the most common basis for digitally produced relief maps.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Levee"" title=""Levee"">dike</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#levee""><span title=""See entry on this page at § levee"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">levee</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distance_decay"" title=""Distance decay"">distance decay</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The decrease in cultural or spatial interactions between two places as the distance between them increases. This effect may be noticeable in <a href=""#town""><span title=""See entry on this page at § town"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">towns</span></a> and <a href=""#city""><span title=""See entry on this page at § city"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cities</span></a>, where certain descriptive characteristics such as pedestrian traffic, building height, and land value tend to decline with greater distance from the <a href=""#city_center""><span title=""See entry on this page at § city center"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">city center</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distributary"" title=""Distributary"">distributary</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A <a href=""#stream""><span title=""See entry on this page at § stream"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">stream</span></a> or <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a> that <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/River_bifurcation"" title=""River bifurcation"">branches off</a> and flows away from a <a href=""#main_stem""><span title=""See entry on this page at § main stem"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">main channel</span></a>. Distributaries are common near <a href=""#delta""><span title=""See entry on this page at § delta"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river deltas</span></a>. Contrast <i><a href=""#tributary""><span title=""See entry on this page at § tributary"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">tributary</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/District"" title=""District"">district</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Geography-Terms-FlashcardsFlashcards/"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a hrefhttps://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_geography_termsGlossary_of_physics"">""Glossary georgraphy terms physics""</> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dome_(geology)"" title=""Dome (geology)"">dome</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;A steep-sided <a href=""#mound""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mound"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mound</span></a> that forms when very viscous lava is extruded from a <a href=""#volcanic_vent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volcanic vent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volcanic vent</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-9"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;An uplifted area of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sedimentary_rock"" title=""Sedimentary rock"">sedimentary rock</a> with a downward dip in all directions, often caused by molten rock material pushing upward from below. The sediments have often eroded away, exposing the rocks that resulted when the molten material cooled.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-35"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dormant_volcano"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Dormant volcano"">dormant volcano</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An active <a href=""#volcano""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volcano"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volcano</span></a> that is in repose (quiescence) but is expected to erupt in the future.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-10"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drift_ice"" title=""Drift ice"">drift ice</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called <b>brash ice</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A type of <a href=""#sea_ice""><span title=""See entry on this page at § sea ice"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sea ice</span></a> consisting of multiple <a href=""#ice_floe""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ice floe"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ice floes</span></a> that are not attached to the <a href=""#coast""><span title=""See entry on this page at § coast"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">shoreline</span></a> or any other fixed object such as a <a href=""#shoal""><span title=""See entry on this page at § shoal"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">shoal</span></a>, and which are therefore free to ""drift"" under the influence of winds and <a href=""#ocean_current""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ocean current"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ocean currents</span></a>. Contrast <i><a href=""#fast_ice""><span title=""See entry on this page at § fast ice"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">fast ice</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drainage_basin"" title=""Drainage basin"">drainage basin</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>catchment area</b>, <b>drainage area</b>, <b>river basin</b>, <b>water basin</b>, or <b>watershed</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">Any area of land where precipitation collects and drains into a common outlet, such as a <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a>, <a href=""#lake""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lake"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lake</span></a>, <a href=""#ocean""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ocean"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ocean</span></a>, or any other <a href=""#body_of_water""><span title=""See entry on this page at § body of water"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">body of water</span></a>. The drainage basin includes all of the <a href=""#surface_water""><span title=""See entry on this page at § surface water"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">surface water</span></a> from precipitation <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface_runoff"" title=""Surface runoff"">runoff</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Snowmelt"" title=""Snowmelt"">snowmelt</a>, as well as all of the <a href=""#groundwater""><span title=""See entry on this page at § groundwater"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">groundwater</span></a> beneath the Earth's surface. Each drainage basin is separated topographically from adjacent basins by a <a href=""#drainage_divide""><span title=""See entry on this page at § drainage divide"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">drainage divide</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drainage_divide"" title=""Drainage divide"">drainage divide</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>water divide</b>, <b>ridgeline</b>, <b>watershed</b>, or <b>water parting</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">The topographical barrier that separates neighboring <a href=""#drainage_basin""><span title=""See entry on this page at § drainage basin"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">drainage basins</span></a>. Divides are often, though not always, located along conspicuous elevated <a href=""#ridge""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ridge"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ridges</span></a> or <a href=""#mountain_range""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mountain range"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mountain ranges</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Draw_(terrain)"" title=""Draw (terrain)"">draw</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>re-entrant</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A terrain feature formed by two parallel <a href=""#ridge""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ridge"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ridges</span></a> or <a href=""#spur""><span title=""See entry on this page at § spur"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">spurs</span></a> with low ground in between them.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drumlin"" title=""Drumlin"">drumlin</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An elongated <a href=""#hill""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hill"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hill</span></a> in the shape of an inverted spoon or half-buried egg which is formed by <a href=""#glacier""><span title=""See entry on this page at § glacier"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">glacial</span></a> ice acting on underlying unconsolidated <a href=""#glacial_till""><span title=""See entry on this page at § glacial till"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">till</span></a> or ground <a href=""#moraine""><span title=""See entry on this page at § moraine"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">moraine</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dry_farming"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Dry farming"">dry farming</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A type of farming practiced in semi-arid or dry grassland areas without irrigation using such approaches as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fallowing"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Fallowing"">fallowing</a>, maintaining a finely broken surface, and growing drought-tolerant crops.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-36"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dry_point"" title=""Dry point"">dry point</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An area of firm or dry ground in a <a href=""#wetland""><span title=""See entry on this page at § wetland"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">wetland</span></a>, <a href=""#marsh""><span title=""See entry on this page at § marsh"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">marsh</span></a>, or <a href=""#floodplain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § floodplain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">floodplain</span></a>, often capable of supporting a human <a href=""#settlement""><span title=""See entry on this page at § settlement"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">settlement</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dune"" title=""Dune"">dune</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A hill of loose <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sand"" title=""Sand"">sand</a> built by the movements and erosional and depositional processes of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wind"" title=""Wind"">wind</a> or water, often occurring in <a href=""#desert""><span title=""See entry on this page at § desert"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">deserts</span></a> and <a href=""#coast""><span title=""See entry on this page at § coast"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">coastal</span></a> areas.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth_science"" title=""Earth science"">Earth science</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called the <b>Earth sciences</b> or <b>geoscience</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;A collective term for the various fields of natural science related to the planet <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth"" title=""Earth"">Earth</a>.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;The branch of science that studies the physical constitution and characteristics of the Earth and its atmosphere, using methods and tools from <a href=""#geography""><span title=""See entry on this page at § geography"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">geography</span></a>, geology, physics, chemistry, biology, and mathematics to build a quantitative understanding of how the Earth works and changes over time.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earthquake"" title=""Earthquake"">earthquake</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The sudden and intense shaking of the ground due to <a href=""#plate_tectonics""><span title=""See entry on this page at § plate tectonics"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">tectonic</span></a> activity.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Hemisphere"" title=""Eastern Hemisphere"">Eastern Hemisphere</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The <a href=""#hemisphere""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hemisphere"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">half sphere</span></a> of the Earth that is east of the <a href=""#prime_Meridian""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Prime Meridian"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Prime Meridian</span></a> and west of the <a href=""#antimeridian""><span title=""See entry on this page at § antimeridian"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">antimeridian</span></a>. It is opposite the <a href=""#western_Hemisphere""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Western Hemisphere"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Western Hemisphere</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Easting"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Easting"">easting</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Geography-Terms-Flashcards/a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_geography_termsof physics""</georraphy terms> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_geography"" title=""Economic geography"">economic geography</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A sub-discipline of geography which studies the location, distribution, and spatial organization of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economics"" title=""Economics"">economic</a> activities across the world.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economies_of_agglomeration"" title=""Economies of agglomeration"">economies of agglomeration</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The economic advantages that accrue to an activity by locating close to other activities; benefits that follow from complementarity or shared public services.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-37"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecoregion"" title=""Ecoregion"">ecoregion</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called an <b>ecological region</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A type of <a href=""#biogeography""><span title=""See entry on this page at § biogeography"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">biogeographic</span></a> province that is smaller than a <a href=""#bioregion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bioregion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bioregion</span></a> and which contains characteristic, ecologically and geographically distinct, and relatively uniform assemblages of biological <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Community_(biology)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Community (biology)"">communities</a> and species. Ecoregion boundaries often overlap within <a href=""#ecotone""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ecotone"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ecotones</span></a> and mosaic habitats, and most ecoregions contain habitats that differ from those described for their assigned <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biome"" title=""Biome"">biome</a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edge_city"" title=""Edge city"">edge city</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A concentration of businesses, commercial buildings, or retail and entertainment venues situated outside of a traditional <a href=""#downtown""><span title=""See entry on this page at § downtown"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">downtown</span></a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_business_district"" title=""Central business district"">central business district</a> in what was previously a <a href=""#suburban""><span title=""See entry on this page at § suburban"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">suburban</span></a> residential or <a href=""#rural""><span title=""See entry on this page at § rural"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">rural</span></a> area.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edgelands"" title=""Edgelands"">edgelands</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The transitional areas of ""fringe"" space at the boundaries of a <a href=""#country""><span title=""See entry on this page at § country"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">country</span></a>, <a href=""#city""><span title=""See entry on this page at § city"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">city</span></a>, or other artificial geographical entity, often distinguished by a partly man-made, partly natural landscape that is in the earliest stages of human management and organization. Compare <i><a href=""#hinterland""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hinterland"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hinterland</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ekistics"" title=""Ekistics"">ekistics</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The scientific study of human <a href=""#settlement""><span title=""See entry on this page at § settlement"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">settlements</span></a> of all types, incorporating concepts such as regional, metropolitan, and community <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urban_planning"" title=""Urban planning"">planning</a> and dwelling design with the goal of achieving harmony between the inhabitants of a settlement and their physical, social, and cultural environments.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elevation"" title=""Elevation"">elevation</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The height of a point on the Earth's surface with respect to <a href=""#sea_level""><span title=""See entry on this page at § sea level"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sea level</span></a>. Compare <i><a href=""#altitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § altitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">altitude</span></a></i>.<sup id=""cite_ref-OERI_1996_1-7"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-OERI_1996-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emergent_coastline"" title=""Emergent coastline"">emergent coastline</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A <a href=""#coast""><span title=""See entry on this page at § coast"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">coast</span></a> or <a href=""#shore""><span title=""See entry on this page at § shore"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">shoreline</span></a> resulting from a rise in land surface elevation relative to sea level.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-38"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enclave"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Enclave"">enclave</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A tract or territory completely surrounded by and enclosed within the territory of one other state, country, or other political entity. Unlike enclaves, <a href=""#exclave""><span title=""See entry on this page at § exclave"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">exclaves</span></a> can be surrounded by more than one other state.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-39"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endorheic_basin"" title=""Endorheic basin"">endorheic basin</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A closed <a href=""#drainage_basin""><span title=""See entry on this page at § drainage basin"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">drainage basin</span></a> that allows little or no outflow to external bodies of water but converges instead into internal <a href=""#lake""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lake"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lakes</span></a> or <a href=""#swamp""><span title=""See entry on this page at § swamp"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">swamps</span></a> which equilibrate through evaporation.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epicenter"" title=""Epicenter"">epicenter</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The point on the Earth's surface directly above the <a href=""#focus""><span title=""See entry on this page at § focus"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">focus</span></a> of an <a href=""#earthquake""><span title=""See entry on this page at § earthquake"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">earthquake</span></a>, near which the seismic waves produced by the earthquake are usually most noticeable.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equator"" title=""Equator"">Equator</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The imaginary circle around the Earth halfway between the geographic poles which is assigned a <a href=""#latitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § latitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">latitude</span></a> of zero degrees and is therefore used as a reference point for all other lines of latitude. It is the largest circumference of the Earth.<sup id=""cite_ref-OERI_1996_1-8"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-OERI_1996-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glacial_erratic"" title=""Glacial erratic"">erratic</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A boulder that has been carried from its source by a <a href=""#glacier""><span title=""See entry on this page at § glacier"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">glacier</span></a> and deposited as the glacier melted. Such boulders are often of different rock types than the surrounding rocks.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-40"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Escarpment"" title=""Escarpment"">escarpment</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A long <a href=""#cliff""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cliff"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cliff</span></a> or steep slope separating two comparatively level or more gently sloping surfaces and resulting from erosion or faulting.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-41"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Esker"" title=""Esker"">esker</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called an <b>os</b> or spelled <b>eskar</b> or <b>eschar</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A long, winding ridge of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stratum"" title=""Stratum"">stratified</a> sand and gravel, usually occurring in <a href=""#glacier""><span title=""See entry on this page at § glacier"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">glaciated</span></a> or formerly glaciated areas.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estuary"" title=""Estuary"">estuary</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The broad lower course of a <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a> where it enters the ocean and is affected by the <a href=""#tide""><span title=""See entry on this page at § tide"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">tides</span></a>. Compare <i><a href=""#delta""><span title=""See entry on this page at § delta"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">delta</span></a></i>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-42"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Etchplain"" title=""Etchplain"">etchplain</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A <a href=""#plain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § plain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">plain</span></a> beneath which the <a href=""#bedrock""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bedrock"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bedrock</span></a> has been subjected to considerable subsurface <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weathering"" title=""Weathering"">weathering</a>, known as ""etching"". Erosion of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regolith"" title=""Regolith"">regolith</a> overlying an etchplain often exposes topographical irregularities such as <a href=""#inselberg""><span title=""See entry on this page at § inselberg"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">inselbergs</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evapotranspiration"" title=""Evapotranspiration"">evapotranspiration</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The process by which water is lost from an area through the combined effects of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evaporation"" title=""Evaporation"">evaporation</a> from the ground surface and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transpiration"" title=""Transpiration"">transpiration</a> from vegetation.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-43"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pothole_(landform)"" title=""Pothole (landform)"">evorsion</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#pothole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pothole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pothole</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exclave"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Exclave"">exclave</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A portion of a state or territory that is geographically separated from the main part by surrounding foreign territory of one or more other states or political entities. Many exclaves are also <a href=""#enclave""><span title=""See entry on this page at § enclave"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">enclaves</span></a>.</dd>
"
"exotic stream"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A <a href=""#stream""><span title=""See entry on this page at § stream"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">stream</span></a> found in an area that is too dry to have spawned such a flow. The flow originates in some moister section.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-44"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extinct_volcano"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Extinct volcano"">extinct volcano</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A <a href=""#volcano""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volcano"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volcano</span></a> that is not expected to erupt again.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-11"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exurban"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Exurban"">exurban</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An adjective describing a region or district that lies outside a <a href=""#city""><span title=""See entry on this page at § city"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">city</span></a> and usually beyond its <a href=""#suburban""><span title=""See entry on this page at § suburban"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">suburbs</span></a>; a place of this type is called an <i>exurb</i>. Compare <i><a href=""#rural""><span title=""See entry on this page at § rural"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">rural</span></a></i>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-45"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_line"" title=""Fall line"">fall line</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geomorphology"" title=""Geomorphology"">geomorphologic</a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unconformity"" title=""Unconformity"">unconformity</a> between an upland region of relatively hard <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basement_(geology)"" title=""Basement (geology)"">crystalline basement rock</a> and a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coastal_plain"" title=""Coastal plain"">coastal plain</a> of softer <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sedimentary_rock"" title=""Sedimentary rock"">sedimentary rock</a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fallow"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Fallow"">fallow</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Agricultural land that is plowed or tilled but left unseeded during a <a href=""#growing_season""><span title=""See entry on this page at § growing season"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">growing season</span></a>. Fallowing is usually done to conserve moisture.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-46"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fast_ice"" title=""Fast ice"">fast ice</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fault_(geology)"" title=""Fault (geology)"">fault</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A fracture in the Earth's crust accompanied by a displacement of one side of the fracture.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-47"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fault-block_mountain"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Fault-block mountain"">fault-block mountain</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A mountain mass created by either the uplift of land between faults or the subsidence of land outside the faults.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-48"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fault_zone"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Fault zone"">fault zone</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An area of numerous fractures in the Earth's crust along which movement has occurred. The movement may be in any direction and involve material on either or both sides of the fractures.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-49"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federation"" title=""Federation"">federation</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A form of government in which powers and functions are divided between a central government and a number of political subdivisions that have a significant degree of political autonomy.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-50"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fen"" title=""Fen"">fen</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
