"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iceberg"" title=""Iceberg"">iceberg</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A large chunk of <a href=""#fresh_water""><span title=""See entry on this page at § fresh water"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">fresh water</span></a> ice which has broken away from a larger body of ice (such as a <a href=""#glacier""><span title=""See entry on this page at § glacier"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">glacier</span></a> or <a href=""#ice_shelf""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ice shelf"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ice shelf</span></a>) and is floating freely in open water.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Igneous_rock"" title=""Igneous rock"">igneous rock</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Rock formed when molten (melted) materials harden.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-65"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Impact_crater"" title=""Impact crater"">impact crater</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A type of <a href=""#crater""><span title=""See entry on this page at § crater"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">crater</span></a> formed by the hypervelocity collision of a solid astronomical body, such as a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meteor"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Meteor"">meteor</a>, with the Earth's surface. Unlike <a href=""#volcanic_crater""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volcanic crater"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volcanic craters</span></a>, impact craters typically have raised rims higher in elevation and depressed floors lower in elevation than the surrounding terrain.</dd>
"
"impoundment"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;Another name for a <a href=""#dam""><span title=""See entry on this page at § dam"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">dam</span></a> that impounds a <a href=""#body_of_water""><span title=""See entry on this page at § body of water"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">body of water</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;The <a href=""#reservoir""><span title=""See entry on this page at § reservoir"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">reservoir</span></a> created by such a dam.</dd>
"
"Inertia Costs of Location"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Costs borne by an activity because it remains located at its original site, even though the distributions of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supply_and_demand"" title=""Supply and demand"">supply and demand</a> have changed.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-66"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inlet"" title=""Inlet"">inlet</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An indentation of a <a href=""#shore""><span title=""See entry on this page at § shore"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">shoreline</span></a>, usually long and narrow, which often leads to an enclosed body of <a href=""#salt_water""><span title=""See entry on this page at § salt water"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">salt water</span></a>, such as a <a href=""#sound""><span title=""See entry on this page at § sound"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sound</span></a>, <a href=""#bay""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bay"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bay</span></a>, <a href=""#lagoon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lagoon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lagoon</span></a>, or <a href=""#marsh""><span title=""See entry on this page at § marsh"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">marsh</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inselberg"" title=""Inselberg"">inselberg</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>monadnock</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">An isolated rocky <a href=""#hill""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hill"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hill</span></a>, knob, <a href=""#ridge""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ridge"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ridge</span></a>, or small <a href=""#mountain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mountain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mountain</span></a> that rises abruptly from a virtually level surrounding <a href=""#plain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § plain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">plain</span></a>. Compare <i><a href=""#mogote""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mogote"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mogote</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Island"" title=""Island"">insular</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Of or relating to an <a href=""#island""><span title=""See entry on this page at § island"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">island</span></a>, or suggestive of the isolated condition of an island.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-67"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Integrated_geography"" title=""Integrated geography"">integrated geography</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called <b>integrative geography</b>, <b>environmental geography</b>, or <b>human–environment geography</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">The branch of geography that describes and explains the spatial aspects of interactions between human individuals or societies and their natural environment.</dd>
"
"intercardinal directions"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called <b>intermediate directions</b> or <b>ordinal directions</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">The set of four intermediate directions used in <a href=""#cartography""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cartography"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cartography</span></a> and <a href=""#navigation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § navigation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">navigation</span></a>, each of which is located halfway between a pair of <a href=""#cardinal_directions""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cardinal directions"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cardinal directions</span></a>: northeast (NE), southeast (SE), southwest (SW), and northwest (NW). They are often included in the <a href=""#compass_rose""><span title=""See entry on this page at § compass rose"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">compass rose</span></a> and are used to define further subdivisions such as the <a href=""#secondary-intercardinal_directions""><span title=""See entry on this page at § secondary-intercardinal directions"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">secondary-intercardinal directions</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interfluve"" title=""Interfluve"">interfluve</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A narrow, elongated, and <a href=""#plateau""><span title=""See entry on this page at § plateau"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">plateau</span></a>-like or <a href=""#ridge""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ridge"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ridge</span></a>-like landform between two <a href=""#valley""><span title=""See entry on this page at § valley"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">valleys</span></a>, or an area of higher ground between two rivers in the same <a href=""#drainage_basin""><span title=""See entry on this page at § drainage basin"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">drainage basin</span></a>.</dd>
"
"intermediate directions"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#intercardinal_directions""><span title=""See entry on this page at § intercardinal directions"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">intercardinal directions</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Date_Line"" title=""International Date Line"">International Date Line</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A line of <a href=""#longitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § longitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">longitude</span></a> generally 180 degrees east and west of the <a href=""#prime_Meridian""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Prime Meridian"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Prime Meridian</span></a>. The date is one day earlier to the east of the line.<sup id=""cite_ref-OERI_1996_1-12"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-OERI_1996-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_waters"" title=""International waters"">international waters</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>

"
"intervening opportunity"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The existence of a closer, less expensive opportunity for obtaining a good or service, or for a migration destination. Such opportunities lessen the attractiveness of more distant places.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-68"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intracoastal_Waterway"" title=""Intracoastal Waterway"">Intracoastal Waterway</a> (ICW)"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A system of navigable inland <a href=""#waterway""><span title=""See entry on this page at § waterway"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">waterway</span></a> channels, maintained through <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dredging"" title=""Dredging"">dredging</a> and sheltered for the most part by a series of linear offshore islands, that follows the Atlantic and Gulf Coasts of the United States more than 4,800 kilometres (3,000&#160;mi) from <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston,_Massachusetts"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Boston, Massachusetts"">Boston, Massachusetts</a>, around the southern tip of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Florida"" title=""Florida"">Florida</a>, to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brownsville,_Texas"" title=""Brownsville, Texas"">Brownsville, Texas</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-69"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inverted_river_delta"" title=""Inverted river delta"">inverted river delta</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Island"" title=""Island"">island</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any piece of sub-continental land that is entirely surrounded by water.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islet"" title=""Islet"">islet</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A very small <a href=""#island""><span title=""See entry on this page at § island"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">island</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isopleth"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Isopleth"">isopleth</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any line on a <a href=""#map""><span title=""See entry on this page at § map"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">map</span></a> connecting places of equal value. These values may express physical or natural quantities, such as elevation above sea level (as with <a href=""#contour_line""><span title=""See entry on this page at § contour line"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">contour lines</span></a>), or quantities related to social or economic statistics, such as population, wealth, or transport costs.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isthmus"" title=""Isthmus"">isthmus</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A narrow piece of land <a href=""#land_bridge""><span title=""See entry on this page at § land bridge"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">connecting</span></a> two larger land areas across an expanse of water by which they are otherwise separated.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jurisdiction"" title=""Jurisdiction"">jurisdiction</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;The right and power to apply the law in a particular place or within a defined field of responsibility.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;The geographical area to which such authority applies.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jhum_cultivation"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Jhum cultivation"">jhum cultivation</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called <b>jhoom cultivation</b> or <b>slash-and-burn agriculture</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">Clear-cutting and/or setting fire to an area of land so it can be used for farm cultivation.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jungle"" title=""Jungle"">jungle</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An area covered with dense vegetation dominated by large trees, often tropical.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kame"" title=""Kame"">kame</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An irregularly shaped <a href=""#hill""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hill"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hill</span></a> or <a href=""#mound""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mound"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mound</span></a> composed of sand, gravel, and <a href=""#till""><span title=""See entry on this page at § till"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">glacial till</span></a> which accumulates in a depression on a retreating <a href=""#glacier""><span title=""See entry on this page at § glacier"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">glacier</span></a> and is subsequently deposited on the land surface with further melting of the glacier. Kames are often associated with <a href=""#kettle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § kettle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">kettles</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karst"" title=""Karst"">karst</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An area possessing surface <a href=""#topography""><span title=""See entry on this page at § topography"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">topography</span></a> resulting from the underground solution of subsurface <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Limestone"" title=""Limestone"">limestone</a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dolomite_(rock)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Dolomite (rock)"">dolomite</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-70"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kettle_(landform)"" title=""Kettle (landform)"">kettle</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>kettle hole</b> or <b><a href=""#pothole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pothole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pothole</span></a></b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A shallow, sediment-filled body of water formed by blocks of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ice_calving"" title=""Ice calving"">ice calving</a> from a retreating <a href=""#glacier""><span title=""See entry on this page at § glacier"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">glacier</span></a>, or by draining floodwaters.</dd>
"
"key col"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>

"
"knoll"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#hillock""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hillock"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hillock</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kolk_(bog)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Kolk (bog)"">kolk</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also spelled <b>colc</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;A violently rotating underwater vortex capable of plucking and scouring <a href=""#depression""><span title=""See entry on this page at § depression"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">depressions</span></a> in <a href=""#bedrock""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bedrock"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bedrock</span></a>, which may leave behind distinct pits or lakes known as <a href=""#rock-cut_basin""><span title=""See entry on this page at § rock-cut basin"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">rock-cut basins</span></a> or <a href=""#pothole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pothole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">potholes</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;Another name for a <a href=""#bog_pond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bog pond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bog pond</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lacustrine_plain"" title=""Lacustrine plain"">lacustrine plain</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A nearly level land area formed by the infilling of a <a href=""#lake""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lake"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lake</span></a> with sediment and the complete drainage or evaporation of water from the lake, leaving the deposited sediments behind.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-71"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lagoon"" title=""Lagoon"">lagoon</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A small area of water connected to the <a href=""#ocean""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ocean"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ocean</span></a> but otherwise blockaded by one or more <a href=""#island""><span title=""See entry on this page at § island"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">islands</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lahar"" title=""Lahar"">lahar</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#mudflow""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mudflow"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mudflow</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lake"" title=""Lake"">lake</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A body of water localized in a <a href=""#depression""><span title=""See entry on this page at § depression"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">basin</span></a> and surrounded entirely by land. Lakes are often defined as separate from any <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a> or stream that serves to feed or drain them.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_bridge"" title=""Land bridge"">land bridge</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any piece of land connecting larger land areas that are otherwise separated by water, especially one over which living organisms, such as terrestrial animals and plants, are able to cross and thereby colonize previously inaccessible lands. Land bridges may be created by <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marine_regression"" title=""Marine regression"">falling sea levels</a>, <a href=""#plate_tectonics""><span title=""See entry on this page at § plate tectonics"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">tectonic activity</span></a>, or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post-glacial_rebound"" title=""Post-glacial rebound"">post-glacial rebound</a>. Compare <i><a href=""#isthmus""><span title=""See entry on this page at § isthmus"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">isthmus</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_cover"" title=""Land cover"">land cover</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The physical material present on the surface of the Earth, including categories such as vegetation (grasslands, shrubs, forests, etc.), bare ground, water, asphalt and artificial surfaces, and many others.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Landform"" title=""Landform"">landform</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A natural feature of the solid surface of the Earth. A combined set of landforms makes up the <a href=""#terrain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § terrain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">terrain</span></a> of a given area, and their arrangement in a landscape is known as <a href=""#topography""><span title=""See entry on this page at § topography"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">topography</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Landmark"" title=""Landmark"">landmark</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any natural or artificial feature that is recognizable enough to be used for <a href=""#navigation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § navigation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">navigation</span></a>; a feature that stands out enough from its environment to be visible across long distances.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Landmass"" title=""Landmass"">landmass</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any large contiguous area of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land"" title=""Land"">land</a> surrounded by <a href=""#ocean""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ocean"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ocean</span></a>. Compare <i><a href=""#continent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § continent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">continent</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lateral_blast"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Lateral blast"">lateral blast</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A sideways-directed explosion from the side or summit of a <a href=""#volcano""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volcano"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volcano</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-17"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latitude"" title=""Latitude"">latitude</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A measure of distance north or south of the <a href=""#equator""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Equator"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Equator</span></a>. One degree of latitude equals approximately 110 kilometers (68&#160;mi).<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-72"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> <i>Lines of latitude</i>, also called <i>circles of latitude</i>, are the imaginary lines that cross the surface of the Earth in an east-west direction (parallel to the Equator) and measure how far north or south of the Equator a place is located.<sup id=""cite_ref-OERI_1996_1-13"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-OERI_1996-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lava"" title=""Lava"">lava</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The term used for <a href=""#magma""><span title=""See entry on this page at § magma"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">magma</span></a> once it has erupted onto the Earth's surface.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-18"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soil_leaching"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Soil leaching"">leaching</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A process of soil nutrient removal through the erosive movement and chemical action of water.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-73"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leeward"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Leeward"">leeward</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The side of a landmass sheltered from the wind. Contrast <i><a href=""#windward""><span title=""See entry on this page at § windward"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">windward</span></a></i>.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-19"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Legend_(map)#Map_symbology"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Legend (map)"">legend</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A key for understanding the meaning of the symbols or pictures in a <a href=""#map""><span title=""See entry on this page at § map"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">map</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-OERI_1996_1-14"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-OERI_1996-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LEDC"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""LEDC"">LEDC</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An acronym for <b>L</b>ess <b>E</b>conomically <b>D</b>eveloped <b>C</b>ountry.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Levee"" title=""Levee"">levee</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>dike</b>, <b>embankment</b>, <b>floodbank</b>, or <b>stopbank</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">An elongated naturally occurring <a href=""#ridge""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ridge"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ridge</span></a> or an artificially constructed wall or barrier which regulates water levels in areas prone to flooding. It is usually earthen and often parallel to the course of a <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a> or a <a href=""#coast""><span title=""See entry on this page at § coast"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">coastline</span></a>.</dd>
"
"life-cycle stage"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A period of uneven length in which the relative dependence of an individual on others helps define a complex of basic social relations that remains relatively consistent throughout the period.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-74"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithosphere"" title=""Lithosphere"">lithosphere</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The Earth's hard, outermost shell. It comprises the crust and the upper part of the mantle. It is divided into a mosaic of 16 major slabs or plates, which are known as <a href=""#lithospheric_plates""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lithospheric plates"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lithospheric plates</span></a> or <a href=""#tectonic_plate""><span title=""See entry on this page at § tectonic plate"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">tectonic plates</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-20"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithospheric_plates"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Lithospheric plates"">lithospheric plates</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called <b><a href=""#tectonic_plate""><span title=""See entry on this page at § tectonic plate"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">tectonic plates</span></a></b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A series of rigid slabs (16 major ones at present) that make up the Earth's outer shell. These plates float on top of a softer, more plastic layer in the Earth's <a href=""#mantle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mantle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mantle</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-21"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loam"" title=""Loam"">loam</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A type of easily worked, highly fertile <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soil"" title=""Soil"">soil</a> composed of clay, silt, and sand in an approximate ratio of 20:40:40. Loams generally heat rapidly, are well-aerated, and drain neither too quickly nor too slowly.<sup id=""cite_ref-Mayhew_4-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Mayhew-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/location"" class=""extiw"" title=""wikt:location"">location</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A particular point or place in physical space. Compare <i><a href=""#absolute_location""><span title=""See entry on this page at § absolute location"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">absolute location</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Location_theory"" title=""Location theory"">location theory</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A group of theories which seek to explain the siting of economic activities in particular <a href=""#location""><span title=""See entry on this page at § location"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">locations</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loess"" title=""Loess"">loess</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A soil made up of small particles that were transported by the wind to their present location.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-75"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Longitude"" title=""Longitude"">longitude</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A measure of distance east or west of <a href=""#prime_Meridian""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Prime Meridian"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">a line</span></a> drawn between the <a href=""#north_Geographic_Pole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § North Geographic Pole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">North</span></a> and <a href=""#south_Geographic_Pole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § South Geographic Pole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">South Poles</span></a> and passing through the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Observatory,_Greenwich"" title=""Royal Observatory, Greenwich"">Royal Observatory</a> at <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greenwich,_England"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Greenwich, England"">Greenwich, England</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-76"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> <i>Lines of longitude</i>, also called <i>meridians</i>, are the imaginary lines that cross the surface of the Earth in a north-south direction (parallel to the Prime Meridian) and measure how far east or west of the Prime Meridian a place is located.<sup id=""cite_ref-OERI_1996_1-15"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-OERI_1996-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Longshore_drift"" title=""Longshore drift"">longshore drift</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Geography-Terms-Flashcards/a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_geography_termsof physics""</georraphy terms> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lowland"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Lowland"">lowland</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any area of land that is lower in <a href=""#elevation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § elevation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">elevation</span></a> relative to another area. The term is often used as a conditional descriptor to distinguish related <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Habitat"" title=""Habitat"">habitats</a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecosystem"" title=""Ecosystem"">ecosystems</a>, especially freshwater <a href=""#riparian_area""><span title=""See entry on this page at § riparian area"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">riparian areas</span></a>, on the basis of elevation above sea level. Lowland areas are usually relatively flat and characterized by slow-flowing waterways and <a href=""#alluvial_plain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § alluvial plain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">alluvial plains</span></a>. Contrast <i><a href=""#upland""><span title=""See entry on this page at § upland"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">upland</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maar"" title=""Maar"">maar</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A broad, shallow, flat-bottomed <a href=""#volcanic_crater""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volcanic crater"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volcanic crater</span></a> created by an eruption involving <a href=""#groundwater""><span title=""See entry on this page at § groundwater"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">groundwater</span></a> coming into contact with <a href=""#magma""><span title=""See entry on this page at § magma"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">magma</span></a>. Maars commonly have low rims and subtle <a href=""#terrain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § terrain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">relief</span></a> and characteristically fill with water to form <a href=""#crater_lake""><span title=""See entry on this page at § crater lake"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">crater lakes</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machair"" title=""Machair"">machair</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magma"" title=""Magma"">magma</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Molten rock containing liquids, crystals, and dissolved gases that forms within the upper part of the Earth's mantle and crust. When erupted onto the Earth's surface, it is called <a href=""#lava""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lava"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lava</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-22"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnetic_north"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Magnetic north"">magnetic north</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The direction a <a href=""#compass""><span title=""See entry on this page at § compass"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">compass</span></a> points, towards the <a href=""#north_Magnetic_Pole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § North Magnetic Pole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Magnetic North Pole</span></a>. Magnetic north differs from <a href=""#true_north""><span title=""See entry on this page at § true north"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">true north</span></a> and <a href=""#grid_north""><span title=""See entry on this page at § grid north"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">grid north</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Main_stem"" title=""Main stem"">main stem</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>trunk</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">The primary downstream <a href=""#channel""><span title=""See entry on this page at § channel"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">channel</span></a> of a <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a> as contrasted with its <a href=""#tributary""><span title=""See entry on this page at § tributary"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">tributaries</span></a>. Virtually all of the water in a river's <a href=""#drainage_basin""><span title=""See entry on this page at § drainage basin"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">drainage basin</span></a> eventually flows through the main stem.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mainland"" title=""Mainland"">mainland</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A term used to denote a <a href=""#contiguous""><span title=""See entry on this page at § contiguous"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">contiguous</span></a> <a href=""#landmass""><span title=""See entry on this page at § landmass"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">landmass</span></a> or political territory relative to its politically associated but geographically remote <a href=""#outlying_territory""><span title=""See entry on this page at § outlying territory"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">outlying territories</span></a>. It is variously used to refer to the <a href=""#continent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § continent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">continental</span></a> (i.e. non-<a href=""#insular""><span title=""See entry on this page at § insular"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">insular</span></a>) part of a polity relative to its <a href=""#exclave""><span title=""See entry on this page at § exclave"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">exclaves</span></a> or oceanic islands; or to the largest or most politically, economically, and/or demographically significant island within an <a href=""#island_nation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § island nation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">island nation</span></a>. For example, continental <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Europe"" title=""Europe"">Europe</a> is often considered ""the mainland"" relative to the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Isles"" title=""British Isles"">British Isles</a>, while the island of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Britain"" title=""Great Britain"">Great Britain</a> is considered ""the mainland"" relative to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Ireland"" title=""Northern Ireland"">Northern Ireland</a> and the many smaller islands that constitute the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom"" title=""United Kingdom"">United Kingdom</a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Makhtesh"" title=""Makhtesh"">makhtesh</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A deep, closed <a href=""#valley""><span title=""See entry on this page at § valley"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">valley</span></a> (usually drained by a single <a href=""#wadi""><span title=""See entry on this page at § wadi"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">wadi</span></a>) surrounded by steep walls of resistant rock and superficially resembling a <a href=""#crater""><span title=""See entry on this page at § crater"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">crater</span></a>. The term is used primarily in the deserts of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel"" title=""Israel"">Israel</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt"" title=""Egypt"">Egypt</a>.</dd>
"
"mammilated"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Smooth and rounded in appearance, used of various landforms of different sizes from individual rocks to entire landscapes.<sup id=""cite_ref-Mayhew_4-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Mayhew-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mantle_(geology)"" title=""Mantle (geology)"">mantle</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A zone in the Earth's interior between the crust and the core that is 2,900 kilometers (1,800&#160;mi) thick. The lithosphere is composed of the topmost 65–70 kilometres (40–43&#160;mi) of the mantle and the crust.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-23"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Map"" title=""Map"">map</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A picture of a place that is usually drawn to <a href=""#scale""><span title=""See entry on this page at § scale"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">scale</span></a> on a flat surface.<sup id=""cite_ref-OERI_1996_1-16"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-OERI_1996-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Map_projection"" title=""Map projection"">map projection</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A systematic transformation of the <a href=""#latitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § latitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">latitudes</span></a> and <a href=""#longitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § longitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">longitudes</span></a> of locations from the surface of a three-dimensional shape, such as a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sphere"" title=""Sphere"">sphere</a> or an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ellipsoid"" title=""Ellipsoid"">ellipsoid</a>, into locations on a two-dimensional <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plane_(mathematics)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Plane (mathematics)"">plane</a>. <a href=""#map""><span title=""See entry on this page at § map"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Maps</span></a> of locations on the Earth require map projections to represent features in a convenient format that is easy to view and interpret, though all map projections necessarily distort the true properties of the Earth's surface to some degree.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maritime_climate"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Maritime climate"">maritime climate</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A climate strongly influenced by an <a href=""#ocean""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ocean"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">oceanic</span></a> environment, typically found on <a href=""#island""><span title=""See entry on this page at § island"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">islands</span></a> and the <a href=""#windward""><span title=""See entry on this page at § windward"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">windward</span></a> shores of <a href=""#continent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § continent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">continents</span></a>. It is characterized by small daily and yearly temperature variation and high relative humidity.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-77"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marsh"" title=""Marsh"">marsh</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A wetland dominated by herbaceous rather than woody plant species and often found at the edges of lakes and streams, where it forms a transition between the aquatic and terrestrial ecosystems.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Massif"" title=""Massif"">massif</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;Any section of the Earth's <a href=""#crust""><span title=""See entry on this page at § crust"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">crust</span></a> which is demarcated by <a href=""#fault""><span title=""See entry on this page at § fault"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">faults</span></a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flexure"" title=""Flexure"">flexures</a> and tends to retain its internal structure while being displaced as a whole.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;A single large <a href=""#mountain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mountain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mountain</span></a> mass or compact group of connected mountains forming an independent portion of a <a href=""#mountain_range""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mountain range"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mountain range</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meander"" title=""Meander"">meander</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">One of a series of regular <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sinuous"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Sinuous"">sinuous</a> curves, bends, loops, turns, or windings in the main channel of a <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a>, <a href=""#stream""><span title=""See entry on this page at § stream"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">stream</span></a>, or other <a href=""#watercourse""><span title=""See entry on this page at § watercourse"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">watercourse</span></a>. Meanders are produced by the repetitive upstream erosion and downstream deposition of sediments along the banks of a watercourse as the water flows back and forth across the axis of a <a href=""#valley""><span title=""See entry on this page at § valley"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">valley</span></a> or <a href=""#floodplain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § floodplain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">floodplain</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meander_scar"" title=""Meander scar"">meander scar</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>meander scarp</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A typically crescent-shaped incision in a <a href=""#bluff""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bluff"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bluff</span></a> or valley wall formed by the remnants of a dry, abandoned <a href=""#meander""><span title=""See entry on this page at § meander"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">meander</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MEDC"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""MEDC"">MEDC</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An acronym for <b>M</b>ore <b>E</b>conomically <b>D</b>eveloped <b>C</b>ountry.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean_climate"" title=""Mediterranean climate"">Mediterranean climate</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any climate characterized by mild, rainy winters and hot, dry summers, as experienced in the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin"" title=""Mediterranean Basin"">Mediterranean Basin</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-78"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megacity"" title=""Megacity"">megacity</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megalopolis"" title=""Megalopolis"">megalopolis</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A chain of roughly adjacent <a href=""#metropolitan_area""><span title=""See entry on this page at § metropolitan area"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">metropolitan areas</span></a> which have merged into a very large and heavily populated <a href=""#urban""><span title=""See entry on this page at § urban"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">urban complex</span></a>. See <i><a href=""#conurbation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § conurbation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">conurbation</span></a></i> and <i><a href=""#metropolitan_coalescence""><span title=""See entry on this page at § metropolitan coalescence"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">metropolitan coalescence</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megaregion"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Megaregion"">megaregion</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meridian_(geography)"" title=""Meridian (geography)"">meridian</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#longitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § longitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">longitude</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesa"" title=""Mesa"">mesa</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An isolated, relatively flat-topped natural elevation, usually more extensive than a butte and less extensive than a plateau.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-79"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metamorphic_rock"" title=""Metamorphic rock"">metamorphic rock</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Rock that has been physically altered by heat and/or pressure.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-80"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metes_and_bounds"" title=""Metes and bounds"">metes and bounds</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A system of land survey that defines land parcels according to visible natural landscape features and distance. The resultant field pattern is usually very irregular in shape.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-81"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metropole"" title=""Metropole"">metropole</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metropolis"" title=""Metropolis"">metropolis</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A large <a href=""#city""><span title=""See entry on this page at § city"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">city</span></a> or <a href=""#conurbation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § conurbation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">conurbation</span></a> which is considered a significant economic, political, or cultural center for a <a href=""#country""><span title=""See entry on this page at § country"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">country</span></a> or geographic region and/or an important hub for regional or international connections and communications.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metropolitan_area"" title=""Metropolitan area"">metropolitan area</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>metro area</b> or <b>commuter belt</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A region consisting of one or more densely populated <a href=""#urban""><span title=""See entry on this page at § urban"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">urban</span></a> cores (often a <a href=""#metropolis""><span title=""See entry on this page at § metropolis"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">metropolis</span></a>) and its less populous surrounding territories, including satellite <a href=""#city""><span title=""See entry on this page at § city"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cities</span></a>, <a href=""#town""><span title=""See entry on this page at § town"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">towns</span></a>, and intervening <a href=""#rural""><span title=""See entry on this page at § rural"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">rural</span></a> areas, all of which are socioeconomically tied to the core as typically measured by <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commuting"" title=""Commuting"">commuting</a> patterns. A metropolitan area usually comprises multiple <a href=""#neighborhood""><span title=""See entry on this page at § neighborhood"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">neighborhoods</span></a>, <a href=""#jurisdiction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § jurisdiction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">jurisdictions</span></a>, and <a href=""#municipality""><span title=""See entry on this page at § municipality"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">municipalities</span></a>, with its inhabitants sharing industry, housing, and many other forms of infrastructure.</dd>
"
"metropolitan coalescence"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The merging of the urbanized parts of separate <a href=""#metropolitan_area""><span title=""See entry on this page at § metropolitan area"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">metropolitan areas</span></a>; a <a href=""#megalopolis""><span title=""See entry on this page at § megalopolis"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">megalopolis</span></a> is a result of this process.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-82"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"metropolitan state"|"

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mogote"" title=""Mogote"">mogote</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An isolated, rounded, steep-sided <a href=""#hill""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hill"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hill</span></a> composed of either limestone, marble, or dolomite and surrounded by nearly flat <a href=""#alluvial_plain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § alluvial plain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">alluvial plains</span></a>, especially as found in <a href=""#tropics""><span title=""See entry on this page at § tropics"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">tropical</span></a> regions.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mole_(architecture)"" title=""Mole (architecture)"">mole</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A long, massive, man-made stone or earthen structure used as a <a href=""#pier""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pier"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pier</span></a> or <a href=""#breakwater""><span title=""See entry on this page at § breakwater"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">breakwater</span></a>, or as a <a href=""#causeway""><span title=""See entry on this page at § causeway"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">causeway</span></a> between places separated by water, but designed to prevent the free movement of water underneath it (unlike a true pier).</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monadnock"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Monadnock"">monadnock</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#inselberg""><span title=""See entry on this page at § inselberg"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">inselberg</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moorland"" title=""Moorland"">moor</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called <b>moorland</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">An upland habitat and <a href=""#ecoregion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ecoregion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ecoregion</span></a> characterized by low-growing vegetation on acidic soils and generally referring to uncultivated <a href=""#hill""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hill"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hills</span></a> but also including low-lying <a href=""#wetland""><span title=""See entry on this page at § wetland"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">wetlands</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moraine"" title=""Moraine"">moraine</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The rocks and soil carried and deposited by a <a href=""#glacier""><span title=""See entry on this page at § glacier"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">glacier</span></a>. An ""end moraine,"" either a ridge or low hill running perpendicular to the direction of ice movement, forms at the end of a glacier when the ice is melting.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-83"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mound"" title=""Mound"">mound</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any heaped pile of earth, gravel, sand, rocks, or debris, typically with a rounded top and of topographically higher <a href=""#elevation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § elevation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">elevation</span></a> than its immediate surroundings.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mountain"" title=""Mountain"">mountain</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A large <a href=""#landform""><span title=""See entry on this page at § landform"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">landform</span></a> that rises prominently above the surrounding land in a limited area, usually in the form of a rocky peak with great vertical <a href=""#topographical_relief""><span title=""See entry on this page at § topographical relief"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">relief</span></a>; a mountain is generally considered steeper than a <a href=""#hill""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hill"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hill</span></a>. Mountains are formed by <a href=""#volcano""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volcano"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volcanic</span></a> or <a href=""#plate_tectonics""><span title=""See entry on this page at § plate tectonics"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">tectonic</span></a> forces and erode slowly through the actions of rivers, glaciers, and <a href=""#weathering""><span title=""See entry on this page at § weathering"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">weathering</span></a>. Most exist within extensive <a href=""#mountain_range""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mountain range"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mountain ranges</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mountain_pass"" title=""Mountain pass"">mountain pass</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mountain_range"" title=""Mountain range"">mountain range</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A series of neighboring <a href=""#mountain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mountain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mountains</span></a> or <a href=""#hill""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hill"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hills</span></a>, often closely arranged in a line and connected by high ground. Individual mountains within the same mountain range are usually the result of the same <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orogeny"" title=""Orogeny"">orogeny</a>, and often (though not always) share a common form, alignment, and geology.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mouth_(river)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Mouth (river)"">mouth</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;The place where a <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a> or <a href=""#stream""><span title=""See entry on this page at § stream"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">stream</span></a> flows into another body of water, such as a <a href=""#lake""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lake"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lake</span></a> or another river but especially a <a href=""#sea""><span title=""See entry on this page at § sea"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sea</span></a> or <a href=""#ocean""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ocean"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ocean</span></a>. <a href=""#delta""><span title=""See entry on this page at § delta"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Deltas</span></a> and <a href=""#estuary""><span title=""See entry on this page at § estuary"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">estuaries</span></a> occur near the mouths of rivers.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;The lower or downstream end or the most accessible entrance of a <a href=""#valley""><span title=""See entry on this page at § valley"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">valley</span></a>, <a href=""#canyon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § canyon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">canyon</span></a>, <a href=""#ravine""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ravine"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ravine</span></a>, or <a href=""#cave""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cave"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cave</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mudflat"" title=""Mudflat"">mudflat</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>tidal flat</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A type of coastal <a href=""#wetland""><span title=""See entry on this page at § wetland"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">wetland</span></a> consisting of exposed layers of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bay_mud"" title=""Bay mud"">bay mud</a> formed by the deposition of silts, clays, and marine animal <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Detritus"" title=""Detritus"">detritus</a> by <a href=""#tide""><span title=""See entry on this page at § tide"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">tides</span></a> or rivers. Mudflats usually form within the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intertidal_zone"" title=""Intertidal zone"">intertidal zone</a> of relatively sheltered areas such as <a href=""#bay""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bay"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bays</span></a> and <a href=""#lagoon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lagoon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lagoons</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lahar"" title=""Lahar"">mudflow</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>debris flow</b> or <b>lahar</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A flowing mixture of water and debris (intermediate between a <a href=""#volcanic_avalanche""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volcanic avalanche"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volcanic avalanche</span></a> and a water <a href=""#flood""><span title=""See entry on this page at § flood"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">flood</span></a>) that forms on the slopes of a <a href=""#volcano""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volcano"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volcano</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-24"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multilingual"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Multilingual"">multilingual</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The ability to use more than one language when speaking or writing. This term often refers to the presence of more than two populations of significant size within a single political unit, each group speaking a different language as their primary language.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-84"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Municipal_corporation"" title=""Municipal corporation"">municipal corporation</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Geography-Terms-Flashcardsimprove the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_geography_termsmaking a contribution georgraphy terms <a href=""https://twitter.com/arigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Municipality"" title=""Municipality"">municipality</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A type of general-purpose <a href=""#urban""><span title=""See entry on this page at § urban"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">urban</span></a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Administrative_division"" title=""Administrative division"">administrative subdivision</a> having <a href=""#municipal_corporation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § municipal corporation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">corporate</span></a> status and powers of self-government or <a href=""#jurisdiction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § jurisdiction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">jurisdiction</span></a> as granted by national and/or state laws to which it is subordinate. Municipalities are often included within but usually distinguished from larger administrative divisions such as <a href=""#county""><span title=""See entry on this page at § county"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">counties</span></a>, though the nature of their territorial boundaries and political jurisdictions can vary considerably in different parts of the world.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muskeg"" title=""Muskeg"">muskeg</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Another name for a <a href=""#bog""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bog"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bog</span></a>, used primarily in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alaska"" title=""Alaska"">Alaska</a> and western <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canada"" title=""Canada"">Canada</a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nadir"" title=""Nadir"">nadir</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Narrows"" title=""Narrows"">narrows</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>narrow</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A land or water passage that is confined or restricted by its narrow breadth, often a <a href=""#strait""><span title=""See entry on this page at § strait"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">strait</span></a> or a <a href=""#water_gap""><span title=""See entry on this page at § water gap"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">water gap</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nation"" title=""Nation"">nation</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A stable community of people formed on the basis of a common geographic territory, language, economy, ethnicity, or psychological make-up as manifested in a common <a href=""#culture""><span title=""See entry on this page at § culture"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">culture</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_mapping_agency"" title=""National mapping agency"">national mapping agency</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A governmental agency which manages, produces, and publishes <a href=""#topographic_map""><span title=""See entry on this page at § topographic map"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">topographic maps</span></a>, geographic data, and sometimes <a href=""#cadastre""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cadastre"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cadastral</span></a> information that is specific to an individual <a href=""#nation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § nation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">nation</span></a> or political territory, such as the United Kingdom's <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ordnance_Survey"" title=""Ordnance Survey"">Ordnance Survey</a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_park"" title=""National park"">national park</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
