"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_landscape"" title=""Natural landscape"">natural landscape</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The original landscape that exists before it is acted upon by humans. Contrast <i><a href=""#cultural_landscape""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cultural landscape"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cultural landscape</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Navigation"" title=""Navigation"">navigation</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;The determination of position and direction, generally by comparing the navigator's position to known locations or patterns.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;The process of monitoring and controlling the movement of a vehicle or craft from one place to another.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neighborhood"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Neighborhood"">neighborhood</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Often abbreviated to <b>hood</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A geographically localized <a href=""#community""><span title=""See entry on this page at § community"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">community</span></a> within a larger <a href=""#city""><span title=""See entry on this page at § city"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">city</span></a>, <a href=""#town""><span title=""See entry on this page at § town"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">town</span></a>, <a href=""#suburban""><span title=""See entry on this page at § suburban"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">suburb</span></a>, or <a href=""#rural""><span title=""See entry on this page at § rural"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">rural</span></a> area, particularly one which supports considerable face-to-face interactions between residents.</dd>
"
"nodal region"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A region characterized by a set of places connected to another place by lines of communication or movement.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-85"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Pole"" title=""North Pole"">North Geographic Pole</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called the <b>Geographic North Pole</b>, <b>Geographic North</b>, or simply the <b>North Pole</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">The point in the <a href=""#northern_Hemisphere""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Northern Hemisphere"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Northern Hemisphere</span></a> where the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth%27s_rotation"" title=""Earth&#39;s rotation"">Earth's axis of rotation</a> meets its surface. It is the northernmost point on Earth, directly opposite the <a href=""#south_Geographic_Pole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § South Geographic Pole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">South Geographic Pole</span></a>, and defines the direction of <a href=""#true_north""><span title=""See entry on this page at § true north"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">true north</span></a> at a <a href=""#latitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § latitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">latitude</span></a> of 90 degrees North; its <a href=""#longitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § longitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">longitude</span></a> can be assigned any degree value. Unlike the South Pole, the North Pole is not located on a continental landmass but in the middle of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arctic_Ocean"" title=""Arctic Ocean"">Arctic Ocean</a>. See also <i><a href=""#north_Magnetic_Pole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § North Magnetic Pole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">North Magnetic Pole</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geomagnetic_poles"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Geomagnetic poles"">North Geomagnetic Pole</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called the <b>Geomagnetic North Pole</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">The point in the <a href=""#northern_Hemisphere""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Northern Hemisphere"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Northern Hemisphere</span></a> where the axis of a theoretical simplified <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dipole"" title=""Dipole"">dipole</a> passing through the center of the Earth would intersect the Earth's surface. It is <a href=""#antipodes""><span title=""See entry on this page at § antipodes"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">antipodal</span></a> to the <a href=""#south_Geomagnetic_Pole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § South Geomagnetic Pole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">South Geomagnetic Pole</span></a>. Because of the fluid nature of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth%27s_core"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Earth&#39;s core"">Earth's molten core</a>, the true axis of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth%27s_magnetic_field"" title=""Earth&#39;s magnetic field"">Earth's magnetic field</a> is not a perfect dipole, and so the Geomagnetic Poles and the actual <a href=""#north_Magnetic_Pole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § North Magnetic Pole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Magnetic Poles</span></a> lie some distance apart.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Magnetic_Pole"" title=""North Magnetic Pole"">North Magnetic Pole</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called the <b>Magnetic North Pole</b> or <b>Magnetic North</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">The point in the <a href=""#northern_Hemisphere""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Northern Hemisphere"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Northern Hemisphere</span></a> at which the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth%27s_magnetic_field"" title=""Earth&#39;s magnetic field"">Earth's magnetic field</a> points vertically downward. It is close to but distinct from the <a href=""#north_Geographic_Pole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § North Geographic Pole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Geographic North Pole</span></a> and the <a href=""#north_Geomagnetic_Pole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § North Geomagnetic Pole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Geomagnetic North Pole</span></a>, and its precise location varies considerably over time due to frequent magnetic changes in the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth%27s_core"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Earth&#39;s core"">Earth's core</a>. Its counterpart in the Southern Hemisphere is the <a href=""#south_Magnetic_Pole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § South Magnetic Pole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">South Magnetic Pole</span></a>, though the two poles are not directly opposite each other.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere"" title=""Northern Hemisphere"">Northern Hemisphere</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The <a href=""#hemisphere""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hemisphere"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">half sphere</span></a> of the Earth that is north of the <a href=""#equator""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Equator"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Equator</span></a>. It is opposite the <a href=""#southern_Hemisphere""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Southern Hemisphere"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Southern Hemisphere</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northing"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Northing"">northing</a>"|"

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oasis"" title=""Oasis"">oasis</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A combination of a human <a href=""#settlement""><span title=""See entry on this page at § settlement"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">settlement</span></a> and an area of cultivated vegetation in an otherwise desolate <a href=""#desert""><span title=""See entry on this page at § desert"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">desert</span></a> or semi-desert environment, made fertile when sources of <a href=""#fresh_water""><span title=""See entry on this page at § fresh water"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">fresh water</span></a>, such as underground <a href=""#aquifer""><span title=""See entry on this page at § aquifer"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">aquifers</span></a>, irrigate the surface naturally or via man-made wells.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ocean"" title=""Ocean"">ocean</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The vast, contiguous body of <a href=""#salt_water""><span title=""See entry on this page at § salt water"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">salt water</span></a> covering more than 70% of the Earth's surface area and surrounding the <a href=""#continent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § continent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">continental</span></a> landmasses, or any portion of this larger body of water that is divided and distinguished from the other portions, each of which is called an ocean, by the presence of the landmasses.<sup id=""cite_ref-OERI_1996_1-17"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-OERI_1996-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ocean_floor"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Ocean floor"">ocean floor</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#seabed""><span title=""See entry on this page at § seabed"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">seabed</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ocean_trench"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Ocean trench"">ocean trench</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A long, narrow, very deep <a href=""#depression""><span title=""See entry on this page at § depression"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">depression</span></a> in the <a href=""#seabed""><span title=""See entry on this page at § seabed"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ocean floor</span></a> where, at the junction of two <a href=""#plate_tectonics""><span title=""See entry on this page at § plate tectonics"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">tectonic plates</span></a>, one plate is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subduction"" title=""Subduction"">subducted</a> steeply beneath the other, often penetrating the <a href=""#mantle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mantle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mantle</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open_range"" title=""Open range"">open range</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A cattle- or sheep-ranching area characterized by a general absence of fences and in which livestock are allowed to roam freely.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-86"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ordinal_directions"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Ordinal directions"">ordinal directions</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#intercardinal_directions""><span title=""See entry on this page at § intercardinal directions"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">intercardinal directions</span></a></i>.</dd>
"

"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orographic_rainfall"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Orographic rainfall"">orographic rainfall</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Precipitation that results when moist air is lifted over a topographic barrier, such as a <a href=""#mountain_range""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mountain range"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mountain range</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-87"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outcrop"" title=""Outcrop"">outcrop</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called an <b>outcropping</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">Any visible exposure of <a href=""#bedrock""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bedrock"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bedrock</span></a> or ancient <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superficial_deposits"" title=""Superficial deposits"">superficial deposits</a> on the surface of the Earth, or more generally, any bare, rocky surface that is topographically distinct from the surrounding <a href=""#terrain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § terrain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">terrain</span></a>. Outcrops occur frequently in places where the rate of erosion exceeds the rate of weathering, such as on steep hillsides and mountains, river banks, and coastlines.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outwash"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Outwash"">outwash</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Rocky and sandy surface material deposited by melted water that flows from a <a href=""#glacier""><span title=""See entry on this page at § glacier"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">glacier</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-88"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overburden"" title=""Overburden"">overburden</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Material covering a mineral seam or bed that must be removed before the mineral can be removed in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strip_mining"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Strip mining"">strip mining</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-89"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxbow_lake"" title=""Oxbow lake"">oxbow</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;A wide U-shaped <a href=""#meander""><span title=""See entry on this page at § meander"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">meander</span></a> in a <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a> or <a href=""#stream""><span title=""See entry on this page at § stream"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">stream</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;The <a href=""#lake""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lake"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lake</span></a> formed when a meander is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meander_cutoff"" title=""Meander cutoff"">cut off</a> from the <a href=""#main_stem""><span title=""See entry on this page at § main stem"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">main stem</span></a> of the river, creating a separate body of water.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/palisade"" class=""extiw"" title=""wikt:palisade"">palisade</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;A wall of wooden stakes used as a defensive barrier.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;A line of bold <a href=""#cliff""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cliff"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cliffs</span></a>, especially one showing <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Columnar_basalt"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Columnar basalt"">basaltic columns</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-90"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salient_(geography)"" title=""Salient (geography)"">panhandle</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#salient""><span title=""See entry on this page at § salient"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">salient</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panhole"" title=""Panhole"">panhole</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>gnamma</b>, <b>weathering pit</b>, and <b>solution pan</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A rounded or circular <a href=""#depression""><span title=""See entry on this page at § depression"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">depression</span></a> eroded into flat or gently sloping cohesive rock, typically shallow and ranging in diameter from a few centimeters to several meters, that is capable of collecting and holding rainwater and snowmelt. The term is sometimes used interchangeably with <a href=""#pothole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pothole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pothole</span></a>, though the latter may also refer to distinct geological features.</dd>

<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peninsula"" title=""Peninsula"">peninsula</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A piece of land surrounded by water along the majority of its border while still being connected to a <a href=""#mainland""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mainland"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mainland</span></a> from which it extends.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permafrost"" title=""Permafrost"">permafrost</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A permanently frozen layer of soil;<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-91"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> permanently frozen ground at high <a href=""#latitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § latitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">latitude</span></a> and high <a href=""#elevation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § elevation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">elevation</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-25"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photogrammetry"" title=""Photogrammetry"">photogrammetry</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;The science and technology of obtaining reliable information about physical objects and environments through the process of recording, measuring, and interpreting photographic images (usually aerial or orbital ones) and patterns of electromagnetic radiant imagery and other phenomena.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;The science of extracting three-dimensional measurements from two-dimensional data, such as images.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physical_geography"" title=""Physical geography"">physical geography</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called <b>physiography</b> or <b>geosystems</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">The branch of geography that studies processes and patterns in the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_environment"" title=""Natural environment"">natural environment</a>, such as the <a href=""#atmosphere""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atmosphere"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atmosphere</span></a>, <a href=""#hydrosphere""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hydrosphere"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hydrosphere</span></a>, <a href=""#geosphere""><span title=""See entry on this page at § geosphere"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">geosphere</span></a>, and <a href=""#biosphere""><span title=""See entry on this page at § biosphere"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">biosphere</span></a>, as opposed to the cultural or <a href=""#built_environment""><span title=""See entry on this page at § built environment"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">built environment</span></a>. Along with <a href=""#human_geography""><span title=""See entry on this page at § human geography"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">human geography</span></a>, it is one of the two major sub-fields of geography.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physiographic_regions_of_the_world"" title=""Physiographic regions of the world"">physiographic region</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A portion of the Earth's surface with a common <a href=""#topography""><span title=""See entry on this page at § topography"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">topography</span></a> and common morphology.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-92"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physiography"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Physiography"">physiography</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Another name for <i><a href=""#physical_geography""><span title=""See entry on this page at § physical geography"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">physical geography</span></a></i>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-93"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foothills"" title=""Foothills"">piedmont</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called <b>foothills</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;Any geographic region lying or formed at the base of <a href=""#mountain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mountain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mountains</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;In the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeastern_United_States"" title=""Southeastern United States"">Southeastern United States</a>, a broad region extending from the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue_Ridge_Mountains"" title=""Blue Ridge Mountains"">Blue Ridge Mountains</a> to the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlantic_coastal_plain"" title=""Atlantic coastal plain"">Atlantic coastal plain</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-94"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pit_crater"" title=""Pit crater"">pit crater</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>subsidence crater</b> or <b>collapse crater</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A type of <a href=""#crater""><span title=""See entry on this page at § crater"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">crater</span></a> formed by the sinking or collapse of the surface lying above a void or empty chamber. Pit craters are similar to <a href=""#caldera""><span title=""See entry on this page at § caldera"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">calderas</span></a> and are often associated with volcanic activity, but lack the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ejecta"" title=""Ejecta"">ejecta</a> deposits and <a href=""#lava""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lava"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lava</span></a> flows of <a href=""#volcanic_crater""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volcanic crater"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volcanic craters</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Place_identity"" title=""Place identity"">place identity</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plain"" title=""Plain"">plain</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any broad, flat expanse of land that generally does not show significant variation in topography or <a href=""#elevation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § elevation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">elevation</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plate_tectonics"" title=""Plate tectonics"">plate tectonics</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A geologic theory that the bending (folding) and breaking (faulting) of the solid surface of the Earth results from the slow movement of large sections of that surface called plates.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-95"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plateau"" title=""Plateau"">plateau</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <i>high plain</i> or <i>tableland</i>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A large area of relatively flat terrain that is significantly higher in elevation than the surrounding landscape, often with one or more sides with steep slopes.</dd>
"
"platted land"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Land that has been divided into <a href=""#surveying""><span title=""See entry on this page at § surveying"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">surveyed</span></a> lots.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-96"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plumb_line"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Plumb line"">plumb line</a>"|"

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plural_society"" title=""Plural society"">plural society</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A situation in which two or more <a href=""#culture""><span title=""See entry on this page at § culture"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">culture</span></a> groups occupy the same territory but maintain their separate cultural identities.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-97"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polar_circle"" title=""Polar circle"">polar circle</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Either of the two circles of <a href=""#latitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § latitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">latitude</span></a> enclosing the Earth's <a href=""#polar_region""><span title=""See entry on this page at § polar region"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">polar regions</span></a>: the <a href=""#arctic_Circle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Arctic Circle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Arctic Circle</span></a> in the Northern Hemisphere and the <a href=""#antarctic_Circle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Antarctic Circle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Antarctic Circle</span></a> in the Southern Hemisphere.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polar_ice_cap"" title=""Polar ice cap"">polar ice cap</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>polar ice sheet</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">Either of the two very large regions near the Earth's geographical poles that are seasonally or persistently covered in ice, which occurs because high-latitude regions receive less direct solar radiation than other regions and therefore experience much lower surface temperatures. The Earth's polar ice may cover both land and sea, and varies in size seasonally and with long-term climate change. They typically cover a much larger area than true <a href=""#ice_cap""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ice cap"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ice caps</span></a> and are more correctly termed <a href=""#ice_sheet""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ice sheet"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ice sheets</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polar_region"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Polar region"">polar region</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Either of the two high-latitude regions surrounding the Earth's geographical poles (the <a href=""#north_Geographic_Pole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § North Geographic Pole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">North</span></a> and <a href=""#south_Geographic_Pole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § South Geographic Pole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">South Poles</span></a>), which are characterized by frigid climates and extensive <a href=""#polar_ice_cap""><span title=""See entry on this page at § polar ice cap"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">polar ice caps</span></a>. The polar region of the Northern Hemisphere is often simply called the <a href=""#arctic""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Arctic"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Arctic</span></a> and that of the Southern Hemisphere is called the <a href=""#antarctic""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Antarctic"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Antarctic</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pole_of_inaccessibility"" title=""Pole of inaccessibility"">pole of inaccessibility</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Geography-Terms-Flashcardsimprove the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_geography_termsmaking a contribution georgraphy terms <a href=""https://twitter.com/arigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_geography"" title=""Political geography"">political geography</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The study of both the spatially uneven outcomes of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politics"" title=""Politics"">political</a> processes and the ways in which political processes are themselves affected by spatial structures. A sub-discipline of <a href=""#human_geography""><span title=""See entry on this page at § human geography"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">human geography</span></a>, its primary concerns can be summarized as the relationships between people, state, and territory.</dd>
"
"polynodal"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Many-centered.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-98"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polynya"" title=""Polynya"">polynya</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An area of unfrozen seawater surrounded by an otherwise contiguous area of <a href=""#drift_ice""><span title=""See entry on this page at § drift ice"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pack ice</span></a> or <a href=""#fast_ice""><span title=""See entry on this page at § fast ice"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">fast ice</span></a>. Polynyas are often formed along polar coastlines through the action of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katabatic_wind"" title=""Katabatic wind"">katabatic winds</a>, but may also form in the open ocean.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pond"" title=""Pond"">pond</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A natural or artificial <a href=""#body_of_water""><span title=""See entry on this page at § body of water"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">body</span></a> of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standing_water"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Standing water"">standing water</a> that is usually smaller than a <a href=""#lake""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lake"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lake</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populated_place"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Populated place"">populated place</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A place or area with clustered or scattered buildings and a permanent human population (a <a href=""#city""><span title=""See entry on this page at § city"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">city</span></a>, <a href=""#settlement""><span title=""See entry on this page at § settlement"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">settlement</span></a>, <a href=""#town""><span title=""See entry on this page at § town"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">town</span></a>, or <a href=""#village""><span title=""See entry on this page at § village"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">village</span></a>) that is referenced with <a href=""#geographic_coordinate_system""><span title=""See entry on this page at § geographic coordinate system"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">geographic coordinates</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-26"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population"" title=""Population"">population</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A collection of organisms of the same group or species which live in a particular geographical area. In the context of geography, it often refers to a collection of humans and is represented at the most basic level as the number of people in a given geographically or politically defined space, such as a <a href=""#city""><span title=""See entry on this page at § city"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">city</span></a>, <a href=""#town""><span title=""See entry on this page at § town"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">town</span></a>, <a href=""#region""><span title=""See entry on this page at § region"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">region</span></a>, <a href=""#country""><span title=""See entry on this page at § country"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">country</span></a>, or the entire <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_population"" title=""World population"">world</a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_geography"" title=""Population geography"">population geography</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A branch of <a href=""#human_geography""><span title=""See entry on this page at § human geography"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">human geography</span></a> that studies the ways in which spatial variations in the composition, distribution, migration, and growth of <a href=""#population""><span title=""See entry on this page at § population"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">populations</span></a> are related to the nature of places. This often involves factors such as where populations are found and how the size and composition of these populations is regulated by the <a href=""#demography""><span title=""See entry on this page at § demography"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">demographic</span></a> processes of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fertility"" title=""Fertility"">fertility</a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mortality_rate"" title=""Mortality rate"">mortality</a>, and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_migration"" title=""Human migration"">migration</a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Positioning_system"" title=""Positioning system"">positioning system</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Geography-Terms-Flashcardseven better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_geography_terms> by making georgraphy terms contribution and <a hrf=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post-industrial"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Post-industrial"">post-industrial</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An economy that gains its basic character from economic activities developed primarily after manufacturing grew to predominance. Most notable would be quaternary economic patterns.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-99"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pothole_(landform)"" title=""Pothole (landform)"">pothole</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>pot</b>, <b>swirlhole</b>, <b>churn hole</b>, <b>evorsion</b>, <b>rock mill</b>, and <b>eddy mill</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;Any smooth, bowl-shaped or cylindrical hollow, generally deeper than it is wide, that is carved into the rocky <a href=""#streambed""><span title=""See entry on this page at § streambed"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bed</span></a> of a <a href=""#watercourse""><span title=""See entry on this page at § watercourse"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">watercourse</span></a> such as a <a href=""#stream""><span title=""See entry on this page at § stream"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">stream</span></a> or <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a>. Fluvial potholes are created by the grinding action of stones or coarse sediment kept in perpetual motion in the same spot by the turbulence of the current. The term is also used to refer to <a href=""#plunge_pool""><span title=""See entry on this page at § plunge pool"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">plunge pools</span></a> beneath <a href=""#waterfall""><span title=""See entry on this page at § waterfall"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">waterfalls</span></a>, which are created by similar processes. See also <i><a href=""#kolk""><span title=""See entry on this page at § kolk"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">kolk</span></a></i>.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;A vertical or steeply inclined <a href=""#karst""><span title=""See entry on this page at § karst"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">karstic</span></a> shaft in a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Limestone"" title=""Limestone"">limestone</a> deposit.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">3.&#160;&#160;In the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Plains"" title=""Great Plains"">Great Plains</a> of North America, a shallow <a href=""#depression""><span title=""See entry on this page at § depression"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">depression</span></a>, generally less than 10 acres (4.0&#160;ha) in area, occurring between <a href=""#dune""><span title=""See entry on this page at § dune"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">dunes</span></a> or on <a href=""#moraine""><span title=""See entry on this page at § moraine"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">morainic</span></a> relief on a <a href=""#prairie""><span title=""See entry on this page at § prairie"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">prairie</span></a> and often filled by an intermittent <a href=""#pond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pond</span></a> or <a href=""#marsh""><span title=""See entry on this page at § marsh"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">marsh</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">4.&#160;&#160;Another name for a <a href=""#kettle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § kettle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">kettle</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">5.&#160;&#160;Another name for a <a href=""#panhole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § panhole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">panhole</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prairie"" title=""Prairie"">prairie</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A type of temperate grassland ecosystem dominated by a characteristic composition of grasses, herbs, and shrubs, rather than by trees. The term is used primarily in North America, but similar ecosystems can be found across the world.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Precambrian"" title=""Precambrian"">Precambrian rock</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The oldest rocks, generally more than 600 million years old.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-100"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presque-isle"" title=""Presque-isle"">presque-isle</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A <a href=""#peninsula""><span title=""See entry on this page at § peninsula"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">peninsula</span></a> connected to the <a href=""#mainland""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mainland"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mainland</span></a> by an extremely narrow neck of land such that the land at its distal end is very close to being an <a href=""#island""><span title=""See entry on this page at § island"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">island</span></a>. See also <i><a href=""#tied_island""><span title=""See entry on this page at § tied island"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">tied island</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prevailing_winds"" title=""Prevailing winds"">prevailing winds</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The direction from which winds most frequently blow at a specific geographic location.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-27"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Primary_sector"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Primary sector"">primary sector</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">That portion of a region's economy devoted to the extraction of basic materials (e.g., mining, lumbering, agriculture).<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-101"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Meridian"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Prime Meridian"">Prime Meridian</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The imaginary line running from north to south through the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Observatory,_Greenwich"" title=""Royal Observatory, Greenwich"">Royal Observatory</a> in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greenwich,_England"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Greenwich, England"">Greenwich, England</a> which is assigned a <a href=""#longitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § longitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">longitude</span></a> of 0 degrees and is therefore used as the reference point for all other lines of longitude.<sup id=""cite_ref-OERI_1996_1-18"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-OERI_1996-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Promontory"" title=""Promontory"">promontory</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A raised mass of land that projects into a <a href=""#lowland""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lowland"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lowland</span></a> or a <a href=""#body_of_water""><span title=""See entry on this page at § body of water"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">body of water</span></a>. Compare <i><a href=""#headland""><span title=""See entry on this page at § headland"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">headland</span></a></i> and <i><a href=""#cape""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cape"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cape</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protected_area"" title=""Protected area"">protected area</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any clearly defined geographic space in which human occupation or the exploitation of resources is limited or forbidden through legal or other effective means because of the area's recognized natural, ecological, cultural, or historical value.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Province"" title=""Province"">province</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A type of second-level administrative division within a <a href=""#country""><span title=""See entry on this page at § country"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">country</span></a> or <a href=""#state""><span title=""See entry on this page at § state"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">federal state</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychogeography"" title=""Psychogeography"">psychogeography</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Geography-Terms-Flashcards/a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_geography_termsof physics""</georraphy terms> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_land"" title=""Public land"">public land</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any land area held and managed in the public domain by a federal or local government.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pueblo"" title=""Pueblo"">pueblo</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A type of Indian village constructed by some tribes in the southwestern United States. A large community dwelling, divided into many rooms, up to five stories high, and usually made of adobe. This is also a Spanish word for town or village.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-102"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quadrangle_(geography)"" title=""Quadrangle (geography)"">quadrangle</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also abbreviated <b>quad</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A standard division of the Earth's surface area used in <a href=""#map""><span title=""See entry on this page at § map"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">maps</span></a> produced by the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Geological_Survey"" title=""United States Geological Survey"">United States Geological Survey</a>. Quadrangles are four-sided polygons of varying size, depending on the map series; for example, 7.5-minute quadrangles divide the mapped surface into quadrilaterals measuring 7.5 minutes (0.125 <a href=""#degree""><span title=""See entry on this page at § degree"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">degrees</span></a>) of <a href=""#latitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § latitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">latitude</span></a> by 7.5 minutes of <a href=""#longitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § longitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">longitude</span></a>, with each 7.5-minute map showing the <a href=""#topographical""><span title=""See entry on this page at § topographical"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">topographical</span></a> detail within one particular quadrilateral of this size. Because the boundaries of quadrangles are based on lines of latitude and longitude, the northern and southern limits of a quadrangle map are not straight lines, and the eastern and western limits are usually not parallel; the actual surface area covered by each map varies with the latitudes depicted.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quarry"" title=""Quarry"">quarry</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A place from which stone, rock, sand, gravel, slate, or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Construction_aggregate"" title=""Construction aggregate"">aggregate</a> is excavated from the ground. Also sometimes called an <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open-pit_mine"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Open-pit mine"">open-pit mine</a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rail_gauge"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Rail gauge"">rail gauge</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The distance between the two rails of a railroad.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-103"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rain_shadow"" title=""Rain shadow"">rain shadow</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An area on the <a href=""#leeward""><span title=""See entry on this page at § leeward"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">leeward</span></a> (downwind) side of a mountain or mountain range that receives greatly diminished precipitation.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-104"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rainforest"" title=""Rainforest"">rainforest</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any <a href=""#forest""><span title=""See entry on this page at § forest"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">forest</span></a> characterized by abundant rainfall, dense layers of vegetation, and extremely high <a href=""#biological_diversity""><span title=""See entry on this page at § biological diversity"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">biodiversity</span></a>. Rainforests are found in both tropical and temperate regions. The term <i><a href=""#jungle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § jungle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">jungle</span></a></i> is sometimes used to refer to a tropical rainforest.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ravine"" title=""Ravine"">ravine</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A fluvial slope landform of relatively steep sides, sometimes with an intermittent <a href=""#stream""><span title=""See entry on this page at § stream"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">stream</span></a> flowing along the downslope channel. Ravines are typically considered narrower and shallower than <a href=""#canyon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § canyon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">canyons</span></a>, larger than <a href=""#gully""><span title=""See entry on this page at § gully"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">gullies</span></a>, and smaller than <a href=""#valley""><span title=""See entry on this page at § valley"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">valleys</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Re-entrant_(landform)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Re-entrant (landform)"">re-entrant</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#draw""><span title=""See entry on this page at § draw"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">draw</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reference_ellipsoid"" title=""Reference ellipsoid"">reference ellipsoid</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A mathematically defined surface that approximates the <a href=""#geoid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § geoid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">geoid</span></a> for use in <a href=""#spatial_reference_system""><span title=""See entry on this page at § spatial reference system"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">spatial reference systems</span></a> or <a href=""#geodetic_datum""><span title=""See entry on this page at § geodetic datum"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">geodetic datum</span></a> definitions. Because of their relative simplicity, reference ellipsoids are used in geographic applications as preferred surfaces on which <a href=""#geodetic_control_network""><span title=""See entry on this page at § geodetic control network"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">geodetic network</span></a> computations are performed and point coordinates such as <a href=""#latitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § latitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">latitude</span></a>, <a href=""#longitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § longitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">longitude</span></a>, and <a href=""#elevation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § elevation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">elevation</span></a> are defined.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Region"" title=""Region"">region</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An area having some characteristic or characteristics that distinguish it from other areas; a <a href=""#territory""><span title=""See entry on this page at § territory"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">territory</span></a> that is of interest to people, for which one or more distinctive traits are used as the basis for its identity.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-105"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regiopolis"" title=""Regiopolis"">regiopolis</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A <a href=""#city""><span title=""See entry on this page at § city"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">city</span></a> located outside the core of a <a href=""#metropolitan_area""><span title=""See entry on this page at § metropolitan area"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">metropolitan area</span></a> that serves as an independent driving force for political, economic, or cultural development within a larger <a href=""#region""><span title=""See entry on this page at § region"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">region</span></a>. Contrast <i><a href=""#metropolis""><span title=""See entry on this page at § metropolis"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">metropolis</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Relief"" title=""Relief"">relief</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#terrain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § terrain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">terrain</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Topographic_map"" title=""Topographic map"">relief map</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#topographic_map""><span title=""See entry on this page at § topographic map"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">topographic map</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Remote_sensing"" title=""Remote sensing"">remote sensing</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The gathering of information about an object or place from a remote location (i.e. without making physical on-site observations), most commonly by the use of satellite- or aircraft-based electromagnetic sensor technologies.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reservoir"" title=""Reservoir"">reservoir</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called an <b>impoundment</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">An artificial <a href=""#lake""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lake"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lake</span></a> or an artificially enlarged natural lake that is used to store water. Reservoirs are often created by the construction of a <a href=""#dam""><span title=""See entry on this page at § dam"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">dam</span></a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lock_(water_navigation)"" title=""Lock (water navigation)"">lock</a> in a natural <a href=""#drainage_basin""><span title=""See entry on this page at § drainage basin"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">drainage basin</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resource"" title=""Resource"">resource</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Anything that is both naturally occurring and of use to humans.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-106"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Retroreflector"" title=""Retroreflector"">retroreflector</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhumb_line"" title=""Rhumb line"">rhumb line</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>loxodrome</b> or simply a <b>rhumb</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A line drawn on the surface of a sphere (or on an idealized representation of the Earth) which crosses all <a href=""#meridian""><span title=""See entry on this page at § meridian"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">meridians</span></a> of <a href=""#longitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § longitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">longitude</span></a> at the same angle, and which therefore has constant <a href=""#bearing""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bearing"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bearing</span></a> relative to <a href=""#true_north""><span title=""See entry on this page at § true north"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">true</span></a> or <a href=""#magnetic_north""><span title=""See entry on this page at § magnetic north"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">magnetic north</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ria"" title=""Ria"">ria</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The seaward end of a <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a> valley which has been flooded as a result of a rise in sea level.<sup id=""cite_ref-Mayhew_4-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Mayhew-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ribbon_lake"" title=""Ribbon lake"">ribbon lake</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A long, narrow, finger-shaped <a href=""#lake""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lake"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lake</span></a>, especially one found in a <a href=""#glacial_trough""><span title=""See entry on this page at § glacial trough"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">glacial trough</span></a> and dammed by a rock bar or <a href=""#moraine""><span title=""See entry on this page at § moraine"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">moraine</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ridge"" title=""Ridge"">ridge</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An elongated raised landform which forms a continuous elevated crest for some distance, such as a chain of <a href=""#hill""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hill"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hills</span></a> or <a href=""#mountain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mountain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mountains</span></a>. The line formed by the highest points, with only lower terrain immediately to either side, is called the <i>ridgeline</i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Riegel_(glacial)"" title=""Riegel (glacial)"">riegel</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An <a href=""#outcrop""><span title=""See entry on this page at § outcrop"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">outcrop</span></a> of resistant <a href=""#bedrock""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bedrock"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bedrock</span></a> that forms a bar across a <a href=""#glacial_trough""><span title=""See entry on this page at § glacial trough"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">glacial trough</span></a> and often acts as a <a href=""#dam""><span title=""See entry on this page at § dam"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">dam</span></a> to impound the waters of a <a href=""#lake""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lake"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lake</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-Mayhew_4-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Mayhew-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rift_valley"" title=""Rift valley"">rift valley</a>"|"

"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Riparian_rights"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Riparian rights"">riparian rights</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The rights of water use possessed by a person owning land containing or bordering a <a href=""#watercourse""><span title=""See entry on this page at § watercourse"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">watercourse</span></a> or <a href=""#lake""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lake"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lake</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-107"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Riparian_zone"" title=""Riparian zone"">riparian zone</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/River"" title=""River"">river</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A natural <a href=""#watercourse""><span title=""See entry on this page at § watercourse"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">watercourse</span></a>, usually <a href=""#fresh_water""><span title=""See entry on this page at § fresh water"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">fresh water</span></a>, that flows towards an <a href=""#ocean""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ocean"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ocean</span></a>, <a href=""#sea""><span title=""See entry on this page at § sea"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sea</span></a>, <a href=""#lake""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lake"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lake</span></a>, another <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a>, or in some cases into the ground.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Riverine"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Riverine"">riverine</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Located on or inhabiting the banks or the area adjacent to a <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a> or <a href=""#lake""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lake"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lake</span></a>. Compare <i><a href=""#riparian_zone""><span title=""See entry on this page at § riparian zone"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">riparian</span></a></i>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-108"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roadstead"" title=""Roadstead"">roadstead</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
