"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tributary"" title=""Tributary"">tributary</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called an <b>affluent</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A <a href=""#stream""><span title=""See entry on this page at § stream"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">stream</span></a> or <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a> that flows into a larger stream or <a href=""#main_stem""><span title=""See entry on this page at § main stem"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">main stem</span></a> or a <a href=""#lake""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lake"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lake</span></a>, rather than directly into a <a href=""#sea""><span title=""See entry on this page at § sea"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sea</span></a> or <a href=""#ocean""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ocean"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ocean</span></a>. Contrast <i><a href=""#distributary""><span title=""See entry on this page at § distributary"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">distributary</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropic_of_Cancer"" title=""Tropic of Cancer"">Tropic of Cancer</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The northernmost <a href=""#latitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § latitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">circle of latitude</span></a> on the Earth at which the Sun appears <a href=""#zenith""><span title=""See entry on this page at § zenith"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">directly overhead</span></a> at its culmination, which lies approximately 23.4 degrees north of the <a href=""#equator""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Equator"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Equator</span></a>. Its southern equivalent is the <a href=""#tropic_of_Capricorn""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Tropic of Capricorn"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Tropic of Capricorn</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropic_of_Capricorn"" title=""Tropic of Capricorn"">Tropic of Capricorn</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The southernmost <a href=""#latitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § latitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">circle of latitude</span></a> on the Earth at which the Sun appears <a href=""#zenith""><span title=""See entry on this page at § zenith"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">directly overhead</span></a> at its culmination, which lies approximately 23.4 degrees south of the <a href=""#equator""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Equator"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Equator</span></a>. Its northern equivalent is the <a href=""#tropic_of_Cancer""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Tropic of Cancer"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Tropic of Cancer</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropics"" title=""Tropics"">tropics</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called the <b>tropical zone</b> or <b>torrid zone</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">The region of the Earth's surface surrounding the <a href=""#equator""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Equator"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Equator</span></a> and bounded by the Tropic of Cancer (23.4° N latitude) and the Tropic of Capricorn (23.4° S latitude). It is characterized by high annual precipitation and the absence of any significant seasonal variation in temperature. The term is often used more broadly to describe any area possessing what is considered a hot, humid climate.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-134"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/True_north"" title=""True north"">true north</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called <b>geodetic north</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">The direction along the Earth's surface towards the <a href=""#north_Geographic_Pole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § North Geographic Pole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Geographic North Pole</span></a>. Geodetic true north differs from <a href=""#magnetic_north""><span title=""See entry on this page at § magnetic north"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">magnetic north</span></a> and <a href=""#grid_north""><span title=""See entry on this page at § grid north"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">grid north</span></a>, and also very slightly from astronomical true north, which is based on the direction of the north <a href=""#celestial_pole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § celestial pole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">celestial pole</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tundra"" title=""Tundra"">tundra</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A treeless <a href=""#plain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § plain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">plain</span></a> characteristic of the <a href=""#arctic""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Arctic"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Arctic</span></a> and subarctic regions.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-135"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Underpopulation"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Underpopulation"">underpopulation</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Economically, a situation in which an increase in the size of the labor force will result in an increase in per-worker productivity.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-136"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"uniform region"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A territory with one or more features present throughout which are absent or unimportant elsewhere.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-137"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Transverse_Mercator"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Universal Transverse Mercator"">Universal Transverse Mercator</a> (UTM)"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Geography-Terms-Flashcardsn.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_physics"">""Glossary of physics""</a> byhttps://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_geography_terms.com/georgraphy terms"">lt us know</a>!</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upland_and_lowland"" title=""Upland and lowland"">upland</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Sometimes used interchangeably with <b><a href=""#highland""><span title=""See entry on this page at § highland"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">highland</span></a></b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">Any area of land that is higher in <a href=""#elevation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § elevation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">elevation</span></a> relative to another area, especially one that is populated by low <a href=""#hill""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hill"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hills</span></a> or situated atop a <a href=""#plateau""><span title=""See entry on this page at § plateau"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">plateau</span></a>. The term is often used as a conditional descriptor to distinguish related <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Habitat"" title=""Habitat"">habitats</a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecosystem"" title=""Ecosystem"">ecosystems</a>, especially freshwater <a href=""#riparian_area""><span title=""See entry on this page at § riparian area"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">riparian areas</span></a>, on the basis of elevation above sea level. Upland areas are usually characterized by relatively fast-flowing waterways and hilly or rocky terrain. Contrast <i><a href=""#lowland""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lowland"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lowland</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urban_area"" title=""Urban area"">urban</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An adjective describing a settlement with a high <a href=""#population_density""><span title=""See entry on this page at § population density"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">population density</span></a> and a developed <a href=""#infrastructure""><span title=""See entry on this page at § infrastructure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">infrastructure</span></a> of <a href=""#built_environment""><span title=""See entry on this page at § built environment"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">built environment</span></a>; places of this type are variously categorized as <a href=""#city""><span title=""See entry on this page at § city"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cities</span></a>, <a href=""#town""><span title=""See entry on this page at § town"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">towns</span></a>, or <a href=""#conurbation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § conurbation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">conurbations</span></a>, or simply called <i>urban areas</i>. Contrast <i><a href=""#suburban""><span title=""See entry on this page at § suburban"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">suburban</span></a></i>, <i><a href=""#exurban""><span title=""See entry on this page at § exurban"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">exurban</span></a></i>, and <i><a href=""#rural""><span title=""See entry on this page at § rural"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">rural</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urban_geography"" title=""Urban geography"">urban geography</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The sub-discipline of geography that derives from the study of <a href=""#city""><span title=""See entry on this page at § city"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cities</span></a>, <a href=""#urban""><span title=""See entry on this page at § urban"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">urban</span></a> processes, and the <a href=""#built_environment""><span title=""See entry on this page at § built environment"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">built environment</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urban_sprawl"" title=""Urban sprawl"">urban sprawl</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The unrestricted growth of housing, commercial development, and roads (typically of low densities) over large expanses of land, usually within or near an existing <a href=""#urban""><span title=""See entry on this page at § urban"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">urban</span></a> or <a href=""#suburban""><span title=""See entry on this page at § suburban"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">suburban</span></a> area and with little concern for civic planning. It is often considered a type of <a href=""#urbanization""><span title=""See entry on this page at § urbanization"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">urbanization</span></a> and almost always carries negative connotations.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urban_studies"" title=""Urban studies"">urban studies</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The study of the development of <a href=""#city""><span title=""See entry on this page at § city"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cities</span></a> and <a href=""#urban""><span title=""See entry on this page at § urban"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">urban</span></a> areas, especially from historical, architectural, or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urban_planning"" title=""Urban planning"">civic planning</a> perspectives.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urbanization"" title=""Urbanization"">urbanization</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The process by which a human <a href=""#population""><span title=""See entry on this page at § population"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">population</span></a> shifts from <a href=""#rural""><span title=""See entry on this page at § rural"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">rural</span></a> to <a href=""#urban""><span title=""See entry on this page at § urban"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">urban</span></a> residency, the gradual increase in the proportion of people living in urban areas such as <a href=""#town""><span title=""See entry on this page at § town"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">towns</span></a> and <a href=""#city""><span title=""See entry on this page at § city"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cities</span></a>, and the ways in which human societies respond and adapt to this change. Urbanization may be characterized as a specific condition at a set time (e.g. the proportion of the total population or physical area within a given set of towns or cities) or as an increase in that condition over time. It precipitates enormous social, economic, and environmental changes for the planet as a whole.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/vale"" class=""extiw"" title=""wikt:vale"">vale</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Another name for a <i><a href=""#valley""><span title=""See entry on this page at § valley"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">valley</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valley"" title=""Valley"">valley</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;A low area between <a href=""#hill""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hill"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hills</span></a> or <a href=""#mountain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mountain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mountains</span></a>, often with a <a href=""#river""><span title=""See entry on this page at § river"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">river</span></a> running through it.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;A <a href=""#depression""><span title=""See entry on this page at § depression"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">depression</span></a> that is longer than it is wide.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vertical_exaggeration"" title=""Vertical exaggeration"">vertical exaggeration</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A <a href=""#scale""><span title=""See entry on this page at § scale"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">scale</span></a> used in certain <a href=""#map""><span title=""See entry on this page at § map"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">maps</span></a>, such as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raised-relief_map"" title=""Raised-relief map"">raised-relief maps</a>, that deliberately distorts the apparent <a href=""#elevation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § elevation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">elevation</span></a> of the map's <a href=""#topography""><span title=""See entry on this page at § topography"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">topography</span></a> in order to emphasize vertical features, which might otherwise appear too small to identify relative to the corresponding horizontal scale.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volcanic_vent"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Volcanic vent"">vent</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">An opening at the Earth's surface through which volcanic materials (<a href=""#lava""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lava"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lava</span></a>, tephra, and gases) erupt. Vents can be at a <a href=""#volcano""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volcano"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volcano</span></a>'s summit or on its slopes; they can be circular (<a href=""#volcanic_crater""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volcanic crater"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">craters</span></a>) or linear (<a href=""#fissure""><span title=""See entry on this page at § fissure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">fissures</span></a>).<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-37"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viewshed"" title=""Viewshed"">viewshed</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The geographical area that is visible from a particular location. It includes all surrounding points within line-of-sight of the location and excludes points beyond the <a href=""#horizon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § horizon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">horizon</span></a> or obstructed by <a href=""#terrain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § terrain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">terrain</span></a> and natural or artificial objects.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Village"" title=""Village"">village</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A small, clustered human <a href=""#settlement""><span title=""See entry on this page at § settlement"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">settlement</span></a> or community, usually larger than a <a href=""#hamlet""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hamlet"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hamlet</span></a> but smaller than a <a href=""#town""><span title=""See entry on this page at § town"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">town</span></a> and often in <a href=""#rural""><span title=""See entry on this page at § rural"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">rural</span></a> areas, though the criteria for distinguishing a village can vary considerably in different parts of the world.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virtual_globe"" title=""Virtual globe"">virtual globe</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>

"
"volcanic avalanche"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>debris avalanche</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A large, chaotic mass of soil, rock, and volcanic debris moving swiftly down the slopes of a volcano. Volcanic avalanches can also occur without an eruption due to an earthquake, heavy rainfall, or unstable soil, rock, and volcanic debris.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-38"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volcanic_crater"" title=""Volcanic crater"">volcanic crater</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A type of <a href=""#crater""><span title=""See entry on this page at § crater"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">crater</span></a> created by <a href=""#volcano""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volcano"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volcanic</span></a> activity, typically shaped like a bowl and containing one or more <a href=""#vent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § vent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volcanic vents</span></a>. Compare <i><a href=""#caldera""><span title=""See entry on this page at § caldera"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">caldera</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volcano"" title=""Volcano"">volcano</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A vent (opening) in the Earth's surface through which <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magma"" title=""Magma"">magma</a> erupts, or the landform that is constructed by eruptive material.<sup id=""cite_ref-USGS_2010_3-39"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USGS_2010-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wadi"" title=""Wadi"">wadi</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;Another name for a <a href=""#valley""><span title=""See entry on this page at § valley"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">valley</span></a>, used primarily in Arabic-speaking parts of the world.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;A dry, ephemeral <a href=""#streambed""><span title=""See entry on this page at § streambed"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">riverbed</span></a> which contains water only when heavy rainfall occurs.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_gap"" title=""Water gap"">water gap</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A low point or opening in a <a href=""#ridge""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ridge"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ridge</span></a> or <a href=""#mountain_range""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mountain range"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mountain range</span></a> carved by the erosional activity of flowing water and through which water continues to flow in the present day. Contrast <i><a href=""#wind_gap""><span title=""See entry on this page at § wind gap"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">wind gap</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_point_mapping"" title=""Water point mapping"">water mapping</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A collection of data represented as a map showing different aspects related to water supplies.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_pollution"" title=""Water pollution"">water pollution</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The contamination of water by chemical or biological constituents which make it unfit for use.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_table"" title=""Water table"">water table</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The level below the land surface at which the subsurface material is fully saturated with water. The depth of the water table reflects the minimum level to which wells must be drilled for water extraction.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-138"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Watercourse"" title=""Watercourse"">watercourse</a>"|"
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>

"
"watershed"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Another name for a <a href=""#drainage_divide""><span title=""See entry on this page at § drainage divide"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">drainage divide</span></a> or <a href=""#drainage_basin""><span title=""See entry on this page at § drainage basin"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">drainage basin</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Waterway"" title=""Waterway"">waterway</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any <a href=""#body_of_water""><span title=""See entry on this page at § body of water"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">body of water</span></a> that is deep, wide, and slow enough to be <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Navigability"" title=""Navigability"">navigable</a> by watercraft.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wave-cut_platform"" title=""Wave-cut platform"">wave-cut platform</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also called a <b>shore platform</b>, <b>wave-cut cliff</b>, or <b>coastal bench</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">A flat <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erosion_surface"" title=""Erosion surface"">erosion surface</a> along the <a href=""#shore""><span title=""See entry on this page at § shore"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">shore</span></a> of a lake, <a href=""#bay""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bay"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bay</span></a>, or <a href=""#sea""><span title=""See entry on this page at § sea"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sea</span></a> that is formed by the undercutting and eventual collapse of a <a href=""#cliffed_coast""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cliffed coast"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sea cliff</span></a> as a result of repetitive wave action.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weathering"" title=""Weathering"">weathering</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The breaking of rocks into smaller rocks, gradually becoming soil.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Hemisphere"" title=""Western Hemisphere"">Western Hemisphere</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The <a href=""#hemisphere""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hemisphere"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">half sphere</span></a> of the Earth that is west of the <a href=""#prime_Meridian""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Prime Meridian"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Prime Meridian</span></a> and east of the <a href=""#antimeridian""><span title=""See entry on this page at § antimeridian"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">antimeridian</span></a>. It is opposite the <a href=""#eastern_Hemisphere""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Eastern Hemisphere"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Eastern Hemisphere</span></a>.</dd>
"

"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilderness"" title=""Wilderness"">wilderness</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">Any natural environment which has not been significantly developed or modified by human activity, or within which natural processes operate without human interference. Such areas are considered important for the survival of wild plant and animal species as well as for maintaining <a href=""#biological_diversity""><span title=""See entry on this page at § biological diversity"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">biodiversity</span></a> and ecological stability. Wildernesses are often <a href=""#protected_area""><span title=""See entry on this page at § protected area"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">protected areas</span></a>.</dd>
"

"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Windward"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Windward"">windward</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The side of a landmass facing the direction from which the wind is blowing. Contrast <i><a href=""#leeward""><span title=""See entry on this page at § leeward"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">leeward</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_city"" title=""Global city"">world city</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">See <i><a href=""#global_city""><span title=""See entry on this page at § global city"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">global city</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Geodetic_System"" title=""World Geodetic System"">World Geodetic System</a> (WGS)"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A standard <a href=""#geographic_coordinate_system""><span title=""See entry on this page at § geographic coordinate system"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">geographic coordinate system</span></a>, spheroidal <a href=""#reference_ellipsoid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § reference ellipsoid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">reference ellipsoid</span></a> (for raw <a href=""#altitude""><span title=""See entry on this page at § altitude"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">altitude</span></a> data), and <a href=""#geoid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § geoid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">geoid</span></a> (which defines the nominal <a href=""#sea_level""><span title=""See entry on this page at § sea level"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sea level</span></a>) used in <a href=""#cartography""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cartography"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cartography</span></a>, <a href=""#geodesy""><span title=""See entry on this page at § geodesy"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">geodesy</span></a>, and <a href=""#satellite_navigation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § satellite navigation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">satellite navigation</span></a> applications worldwide. The latest revision, <i>WGS84</i>, is the standard coordinate system used by the <a href=""#global_Positioning_System""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Global Positioning System"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Global Positioning System</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_map"" title=""World map"">world map</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A <a href=""#map""><span title=""See entry on this page at § map"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">map</span></a> of most or all of the surface of the Earth.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yardang"" title=""Yardang"">yardang</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">A streamlined protuberance carved from <a href=""#bedrock""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bedrock"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bedrock</span></a> or any consolidated or semi-consolidated material by the dual action of wind <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abrasion_(geology)"" title=""Abrasion (geology)"">abrasion</a> and erosion, especially one found in a <a href=""#desert""><span title=""See entry on this page at § desert"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">desert</span></a>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zoning"" title=""Zoning"">zoning</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The public regulation of land and building use to control the character of a place.<sup id=""cite_ref-IIP_2008_2-139"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IIP_2008-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zenith"" title=""Zenith"">zenith</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">The imaginary point on the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celestial_sphere"" title=""Celestial sphere"">celestial sphere</a> that is directly above a particular location (i.e. in the vertical direction exactly opposite to the apparent direction of the gravitational force at that location). Contrast <i><a href=""#nadir""><span title=""See entry on this page at § nadir"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">nadir</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
